The Definition of al-Hamd: Linguistic and Technical Analysis
Author defines 'hamd' linguistically and technically, with commentary on 'urf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to dissect the linguistic definition of al-hamd into its four components and distinguish it from the technical (urfi) definition.

Core Idea
Al-hamd in the basmala is defined by general custom, not by any science's technical term.

The opening word of the poem is 'al-hamd'. The author first clarifies what 'hamd' means, because its precise meaning affects how we understand the praise. The linguistic definition is carefully structured; the technical definition is simple but must be correctly contextualized. This lesson walks through the components and the important annotation about 'urf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The term being defined is 'al-hamd'. Find where the definition begins and note the two contexts: linguistic (lughatan) and technical (urfan).
The Arabic text starts with 'قد اشتهر أن الحمد لغة'.
2
Extract the four components of the linguistic definition
The linguistic definition has four parts: (1) thana' (praising), (2) bi al-jamil (with beauty), (3) 'ala al-jamil al-ikhtiyari (for the voluntary beauty), (4) 'ala jihhat al-ta'zim (in a manner of exaltation). Write them out and see what each adds.
Each part restricts the meaning; e.g., 'voluntary' excludes non-voluntary actions.
3
Compare with the technical definition
The technical definition is 'an act that indicates exaltation of the Benefactor.' Note how it differs: it focuses on the act itself rather than the speech act of praising. The object is the Benefactor, not the beauty.
The technical definition appears truncated but the key elements are clear.
4
Understand the annotation on 'urf
Ibn Abd al-Haqq clarifies that 'urf here means 'al-urf al-amm' (general custom), not the specific usage of a science like logic or fiqh. This prevents misinterpretation.
This is important because 'hamd' has different technical meanings in different disciplines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الحمد لله) قد اشتهر أن الحمد لغة : الثناء بالجميل على الجميل الاختياري على جهة التعظيم. وعرفاً : فعل ينبي عن تعظيم المنعم من حيث . قوله : (وعرفاً) قال ابن عبد الحق : المراد بالعرف هنا : العرف العام.
His statement: (Praise be to God) — it is well-known that 'hamd' linguistically is: praising with beauty for the voluntary beauty in a manner of exaltation. And technically: an act that indicates exaltation of the benefactor in terms of... His statement: (and technically) — Ibn Abd al-Haqq said: By 'technically' here is meant the general custom.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage defines the word 'al-hamd' (praise) as it appears in the opening of the poem. The linguistic definition consists of four parts: (1) thana' (praising), (2) bi al-jamil (with beauty), (3) 'ala al-jamil al-ikhtiyari (for the voluntary beauty), (4) 'ala jihhat al-ta'zim (in a manner of exaltation). This distinguishes hamd from ordinary praise. The technical (urfi) definition is given as 'an act that indicates exaltation of the Benefactor from where...' but the text is incomplete. The following annotation clarifies that 'urf' here means 'al-urf al-amm' (general custom), not the specific technical terminology of a particular science. This is important because terms like 'hamd' have different technical meanings in different disciplines, and the author wants to use the common understanding.

Key Terms

الثناء
العرف

D) It means the same as 'istilah' in hadith sciences.

Key Takeaway
Al-hamd is defined as praising the voluntary beautiful action with exaltation, and in this text it follows general custom, not a discipline-specific technical term.

Defining al-Hamd: Linguistic and Customary Definitions
Bajuri defines hamd linguistically and customarily, then addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the linguistic and customary definitions of al-hamd and explain how the objection concerning Allah's attributes is resolved.

Core Idea
Al-hamd is reverential commendation extended by analogy to include Allah's essential attributes.

In his commentary on the Basmala, al-Bajuri carefully defines the term 'al-hamd' that begins the Fatiha. He provides a linguistic definition rooted in Arabic usage and a customary definition grounded in practice. He then addresses a potential objection that could exclude praise of Allah's essence. This lesson walks through each definition and the logical move that preserves the comprehensiveness of hamd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition's components
Al-Bajuri states: 'al-hamd linguistically is: commendation (thana') with beauty (al-jamil) upon a voluntary beautiful act (al-jamil al-ikhtiyari) in the manner of magnification (ta'zim).' Break these into: the act of praising, the quality of the praise (beautiful), the object (voluntary good act), and the manner (reverential).
The word 'thana'' alone can include blame, so the qualification 'with beauty' restricts it to good praise.
2
Analyze the customary definition
The customary definition: 'an act (fi'l) that indicates magnification of the Benefactor (ta'zim al-mun'im) insofar as He is a Benefactor upon the one praising or others.' Note that it is an 'act' (could be speech, action) and specifies the Benefactor relation.
This definition focuses on the function of praise as expressing gratitude and reverence toward a benefactor.
3
Locate the objection and its basis
The objector says: 'The restriction with 'voluntary' (ikhtiyari) excludes praise upon the essence and attributes of Allah, since they are not voluntary acts.' This is a logical challenge: if hamd requires a voluntary act, then praising Allah for His essence (not an act) would not be hamd.
This objection is crucial because the Basmala itself praises Allah, so the definition must accommodate that.
4
Analyze al-Bajuri's response
Al-Bajuri answers that 'voluntary' includes both the truly voluntary (sources of acts) and by extension the qualities related to voluntary acts. Allah's attributes are not voluntary in themselves, but they are the source of His voluntary acts, so praising Him for His attributes is included by way of derivation.
This is a logical expansion: the term 'voluntary' is interpreted broadly to cover both actual and originalive voluntary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (الحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ) قَدِ اشْتُهِرَ أَنَّ الحَمْدَ لغةً : الثَّنَاءُ بِالجَمِيلِ عَلَى الجَمِيلِ الاخْتِيَارِيِّ عَلَى جِهَةِ التَّعْظِيمِ. وَعُرْفاً : «فِعْلُ يُنْبِي عَنْ تَعْظِيمِ المُنْعِمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مُنْعِمٌ عَلَى الحَامِدِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ». فَإِنْ قِيْلَ: التَّقْيِيدُ بِـ (الِاخْتِيَارِيِّ) يُخْرِجُ : الحَمْدَ عَلَى ذَاتِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَصِفَاتِهِ. أَجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّ المُرَادَ بـ (الِاخْتِيَارِيِّ) مَا يَشْمَلُ : الاخْتِيَارِيَّ حَقِيقَةٌ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ.
His statement: 'Praise be to Allah' – it is well-known that al-hamd linguistically is: commendation with beauty upon the voluntary beautiful act in the manner of magnification. And customarily: an act that indicates the magnification of the Benefactor insofar as He is a Benefactor upon the one praising or others. If it is said: the restriction with 'voluntary' excludes praise upon the essence of Allah Almighty and His attributes. It was answered: that what is meant by 'voluntary' includes the truly voluntary, which is apparent, and the heir [i.e., what is related to it].
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'al-hamd' (praise) both linguistically and in customary usage. The author, al-Bajuri, begins by stating the well-known linguistic definition: al-hamd is commendation (al-thana') with something beautiful (al-jamil) upon a voluntary beautiful act (al-jamil al-ikhtiyari) in a manner indicating magnification (ta'zim). The phrase 'with something beautiful' means the praise is for a good quality, and 'upon a voluntary beautiful act' specifies that the object of praise is an act done by choice, not a necessary attribute. The qualification 'in a manner of magnification' ensures the praise is reverential. Then al-Bajuri gives the customary definition (al-'urf): al-hamd is an act (fi'l) that indicates magnification of the Benefactor (al-mun'im) insofar as He is a benefactor to the one praising or to others. This defines hamd as a deed (e.g., speech, action) that shows reverence for the giver of favors. He then raises an objection: the restriction 'voluntary' in the linguistic definition would exclude praising Allah's essence and attributes, since they are not voluntary acts. The answer is that 'voluntary' (al-ikhtiyari) here includes both the truly voluntary (like acts of will) and what is considered voluntary by extension (like Allah's attributes, which are sources of voluntary acts). Thus, praising Allah's essence and attributes is still valid hamd.

Key Terms
الحمد
الثناء
الجميل الاختياري
التعظيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, what is the customary definition of al-hamd?
A) Commendation with beauty upon a voluntary beautiful act.
B) An act indicating magnification of the Benefactor insofar as He is a Benefactor.
C) Praise of Allah for His essence and attributes.
D) Speech that thanks a benefactor.

Key Takeaway
Al-hamd is defined as reverential commendation of a voluntary beneficial act, but this is extended to include praise of Allah's attributes as they are the source of voluntary acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the linguistic definition, determine whether the utterance 'الحمد لله على كرمه' is a valid instance of hamd, given that 'كرم' (generosity) is an attribute and not a voluntary act. Support your answer with al-Bajuri's response about extension.
?
Apply the customary definition to a scenario: A person thanks another for a gift, but the other person is not actually the giver (e.g., a messenger). Is this an act of hamd according to the definition? Why or why not?

Proposition Types in 'Al-Ḥamdu Lillāh'
The author classifies 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' by article interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' as a singular, universal, or particular proposition based on the interpretation of the definite article 'al'.

Core Idea
The same sentence can be singular, universal, or particular depending on the article.

In Islamic logic, the basmala is often used as a prime example to demonstrate how the same Arabic sentence can yield different proposition types. This lesson unpacks the three logical interpretations of the definite article 'al' in 'al-ḥamdu lillāh', showing how it shifts from a specific eternal praise to a universal or particular claim. Understanding this helps you see the precision required in theological and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sentence type
First, determine whether 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' is used as a performative (inshā') or a declarative (khabar). Only declarative sentences are propositions (qadiyya).
The passage states it can be either, but we focus on the declarative case for proposition analysis.
2
Examine the definite article 'al'
The definite article in 'al-ḥamdu' can have three meanings: covenant (al-ʿahd), universal (istiġrāq), or genus (jins). Each yields a different proposition type.
This is a key logical distinction that applies to many Arabic phrases.
3
Interpret 'al' as covenant
If 'al' refers to a specific known individual (here, the eternal praise of God), the proposition is singular (qadiyya shakhṣiyya).
This interpretation aligns with theological discussions of the eternal divine speech.
4
Interpret 'al' as universal
If 'al' indicates all individuals of the genus (all praise), the proposition is universal (qadiyya kulliyya).
This is the most common understanding in everyday recitation.
5
Interpret 'al' as genus
If 'al' stands for the genus but refers to some part (fi ḍimni al-baʿḍ), the proposition is particular (qadiyya juziyya).
This interpretation is less common but logically valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِمَّا يَنْبَغِي التَّنْبَهَ لَهُ : أَنَّ الحَمْدَ القَدِيمَ هُوَ نَفْسُ الكَلَامِ القَدِيمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ دَلَالَتِهِ عَلَى الكَمَالَاتِ، فَهُوَ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ الكَلَامِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ ، كَمَا هُوَ مُقَرَّرٌ فِي عِلْمِ التَّوْحِيدِ. وَقَدِ اشْتُهِرَ أَيْضاً أَنَّ جُمْلَةَ الحَمْدَلَةِ يَصِحُ أَنْ تَكُونَ إِنْشَائِيَّةً ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَلَا تُسَمَّى : «قَضِيَّةٌ»؛ لِمَا مَرَّ ، وَأَنْ تَكُونَ خَبَرِيَّةً ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَتُسَمَّى : «قَضِيَّةٌ»؛ ثُمَّ: إِنْ جُعِلَتْ «أَلْ» فِيهَا لِلعَهْدِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ شَخْصِيَّةٌ». وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لِلِاسْتِغْرَاقِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ كُلِّيَّةٌ». وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لِلجِنْسِ فِي ضِمْنِ البَعْضِ ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ جُزْئِيَّةٌ».
And among what should be paid attention to is that the eternal praise is itself the eternal speech with respect to its indication of perfections, so it is from the types of attributional speech, as established in the science of tawhid. And it is also well-known that the sentence of al-ḥamdalah may be performative, in which case it is not called a 'proposition', for what has passed, and it may be declarative, in which case it is called a 'proposition'. Then: if the 'al' in it is made for covenant, it is a singular proposition; if made for universal, it is a universal proposition; if made for genus in the sense of the part, it is a particular proposition.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the commentary on the basmala. It first clarifies that the eternal praise is the same as the eternal divine speech, but considered from its meaning of indicating perfections; this is a technical point in theology (tawhid). Then it discusses that the phrase 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' can be either a performative utterance (inshā') or a declarative statement (khabar). If declarative, it is a proposition (qadiyya). The article 'al' can be interpreted in three ways: for a specific covenant (al-ʿahd), making it a singular proposition (qadiyya shakhṣiyya) because it refers to a specific known individual (God's praise); for universal (istiġrāq), making it a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) meaning all praise belongs to God; or for genus (jins) in the sense of part (fi ḍimni al-baʿḍ), making it a particular proposition (qadiyya juziyya) because it refers to some part of the genus of praise. This demonstrates the logical flexibility of Arabic and the importance of understanding the article's function in determining proposition type.

Key Terms
قضية (qadiyya): A declarative sentence that can be true or false; here used to classify the basmala when taken as a news statement. [Note: Stable term across logic texts, though some authors distinguish it from propositional content.]
أل (al): The definite article; its interpretation (covenant, universal, genus) determines the type of proposition. [Note: In Arabic grammar, 'al' has various functions; here it is specifically analyzed in logical context.]
للعهد (li-l-ʿahd): For covenant: referring to a specific, known individual (here, the eternal praise of God). [Note: No significant shift; standard usage.]
للاستغراق (li-l-istiġrāq): For universal: indicating all individuals of the genus (here, all praise). [Note: No significant shift.]
للجنس (li-l-jins): For genus: indicating the essence of the genus, but here applied to a part (some praise). [Note: In logic, 'al' for genus can yield a particular proposition when modified by 'fi ḍimni al-baʿḍ'.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the definite article 'al' in 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' is interpreted as 'for covenant' (li-l-ʿahd), what type of proposition does it become?
A) Universal proposition
B) Particular proposition
C) Singular proposition
D) Performative utterance

Key Takeaway
The definite article in Arabic can yield singular, universal, or particular propositions, and identifying the correct type is essential for precise logical analysis in Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the phrase 'al-ʿālamūna' (the worlds) in the basmala using the three interpretations of the definite article. Determine what type of proposition it would be under each interpretation (covenant, universal, genus).
?

Distinguishing Muhmala and Tabi'iyya Propositions
Author defines muhmala and tabi'iyya propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given Arabic proposition is muhmala or tabi'iyya based on the treatment of the definite article 'al'.

Core Idea
The same sentence can be muhmala or tabi'iyya depending on whether 'al' refers to individuals or the nature.

This passage introduces two ways to analyze categorical propositions in Islamic logic: indefinite (muhmala) and natural (tabi'iyya). The distinction lies in how we understand the definite article 'al'. The author explains that 'al-hamdu lillah' can be taken as muhmala if considered with respect to individuals, or as tabi'iyya if 'al' indicates the genus of praise. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting logical propositions in Islamic arguments, especially in theological contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject term with 'al'
Locate the subject of the proposition, which typically has the definite article 'al'. For example, in 'al-ḥamdu lillāh', the subject is 'al-ḥamd' (praise).
The subject may be a definite noun; the key is the scope of 'al'.
2
Determine if 'al' is considered with respect to individuals or the genus
Ask: Does 'al' refer to individual instances (indefinite scope) or to the essence/nature (universal)? The author says we can cut off consideration of universality and particularity to treat it as muhmala, or consider 'al' for the genus to make it tabi'iyya.
Both readings are possible; the logician chooses based on context.
3
Classify the proposition as muhmala or tabi'iyya
If 'al' is taken with respect to individuals but without specifying quantity, it is muhmala (indefinite). If 'al' indicates the genus or nature disregarding individuals, it is tabi'iyya (natural).
The author notes that there is no impediment to considering 'al-hamdu lillah' as tabi'iyya in this context.
4
Check for any impediment or contextual clue
Consider whether the intended meaning requires individuality or universality. In the case of 'al-hamdu lillah', the praise is for Allah in His essence, so tabi'iyya is appropriate.
This step ties the logical classification to the actual usage in Islamic discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لَهُ فِي ضِمْنِ الأَفْرَادِ بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الكُلِّيَّةِ وَالجُزْئِيَّةِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ مُهْمَلَةٌ». وَلَا مَانِعَ هُنَا مِنْ جَعْلِهَا طَبِيعِيَّة)؛ بِأَنْ تُجْعَلَ أَلْ» فِيهَا لِلجِنْسِ وَالطَّبِيعَةِ، بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الْأَفْرَادِ. وَاسْتُشْكِلَ كَوْنَهَا إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ : بِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ العَبْدَ أَنْ يُنْشِئَ مَضْمُونَ هَذِهِ الجُمْلَةِ وَلَا حُكْمَهَا : - وَالأَوَّلُ هُوَ : اخْتِصَاصُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالحَمْدِ إِنْ قُدِّرَ الخَبَرُ مِنْ مَادَّةِ الاِخْتِصَاص) أَوِ اسْتِحْقَاقُهُ لَهُ إِنْ قُدْرَ مِنْ مَادَّةِ الاِسْتِحْقَاقِ، أَوْ مُلْكُهُ لَهُ إِنْ قُدِّرَ مِنْ مَادَّةِ المِلْكِ؛ لِأَنَّ مَضْمُونَ الجُمْلَةِ هُوَ المَصْدَرُ المُتَصَيَّدُ مِنَ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ المُضَافُ لِلمَحْكُومٍ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كَانَ المَحْكُومُ بِهِ مُشْتَقًا كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكِ: «زَيْدٌ قَائِمٌ»، أَوِ الكَوْنُ المُضَافُ لِلمَحْكُومٍ عَلَيْهِ مَعْ جَعَلِ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ خَبَراً عَنْ ذَلِكَ الكَوْنِ إِنْ كَانَ المَحْكُومُ بِهِ جَامِداً كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ : زَيْدٌ أَسَدٌ». وَالثَّانِي : ثُبُوتُ مَا ذُكِرَ ; لِأَنَّ حُكْمَ الجُمْلَةِ هُوَ الثُّبُوتُ المُضَافُ لِمَضْمُونِهَا ، وَيُرَادِفُهُ : النِّسْبَةُ، وَالمَعْنَى ، وَالمَفْهُومُ . وَأُجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ المُرَادُ بِـ كَوْنِهَا إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ» : كَوْنَهَا لِإِنْشَاء مَضْمُونَهَا أَوْ حُكْمَهَا، بَلْ كَوْنُهَا لِإِنْشَاءِ الثَّنَاءِ بِذَلِكَ . وَالكَلَامُ عَلَى الحَمْدَلَةِ قَدْ شَاعَ وَذَاعَ، فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى ذِكْرِهِ
And if it is made for it within individuals, cutting off consideration of universality and particularity, it is an 'indefinite proposition'. And there is no impediment here to making it natural, by making 'al' in it for the genus and nature, cutting off consideration of individuals. And it was objected that it is declarative (insha'iyya): that the servant cannot create the content of this sentence nor its judgment. The first is: the specification of Allah, Exalted, with praise, if the predicate is estimated from the matter of specification, or His deserving it if estimated from the matter of deserving, or His ownership of it if estimated from the matter of ownership; because the content of the sentence is the verbal noun extracted from the predicate added to the subject, if the predicate is derived, as in your saying: 'Zayd is standing', or the existence added to the subject with making the predicate a predicate of that existence, if the predicate is solid (jāmid), as in your saying: 'Zayd is a lion'. And the second: the establishment of what was mentioned; because the judgment of the sentence is the establishment added to its content, and synonymous with it are: relation, meaning, and concept. And it was answered: that what is meant by its being 'insha'iyya' is not its being for creating its content or its judgment, but its being for creating praise by that. And talk about the hamdalah has become widespread and well-known, so there is no need to mention it.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage defines two types of propositions depending on the treatment of the definite article 'al' and then addresses an objection regarding the insha'iyya nature of 'al-hamdu lillah'. The author begins by explaining that if a proposition like 'al-hamdu lillah' is considered with respect to individuals, disregarding universality and particularity, it is called an 'indefinite proposition' (qadiyya muhmala). However, if the 'al' is taken to indicate the genus or nature, disregarding individuals, it becomes a 'natural proposition' (qadiyya tabi'iyya). The author clarifies that there is no impediment to considering it natural in this context because the intended meaning is the affirmation of praise as a right, which holds regardless of individuals. The text then raises an objection: 'al-hamdu lillah' cannot be a declarative (insha'iyya) sentence because the servant cannot create its content or its judgment. The content (madhmūn) is explained: if the predicate is derived, the content is the verbal noun extracted from the predicate attributed to the subject (e.g., 'Zayd’s standing'), and if the predicate is a solid noun (jāmid), the content is the existence attributed to the subject with the predicate as a predicate of that existence (e.g., 'Zayd’s lionness'). The judgment (hukm) of the sentence is the affirmation (thubūt) of that content, also called relation (nisba), meaning (ma'nā), or concept (mafhūm). The answer to the objection is that 'insha'iyya' here does not mean creating the content or judgment, but creating praise (thanā') by means of that sentence. The commentator concludes that the topic of the hamdalah is widespread, so no further elaboration is needed. This passage illustrates the precision of logicians in analyzing sentence components and their types, distinguishing between the content, judgment, and the act of uttering the sentence.

Key Terms
قضية مهملة
قضية طبيعية

Checkpoint

A) A proposition where 'al' indicates the genus or nature, disregarding individuals.
B) A proposition where the subject is considered with respect to individuals without specifying universality or particularity.
C) A proposition that is always particular in scope.
D) A proposition that is equivalent to a universal affirmative.

Key Takeaway
A proposition can be classified as muhmala (indefinite) or tabi'iyya (natural) based on whether the definite article 'al' is taken to refer to individuals or to the genus and nature.

What Is Mantiq?

Resolving the Insha'iyya Objection on 'Al-hamdu lillah'
Author answers an objection about the insha'iyya nature of 'al-hamdu lillah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'al-hamdu lillah' is considered insha'iyya despite not creating its content or judgment, by distinguishing between creating the content/judgment and creating praise.

Core Idea
The servant creates praise by uttering 'al-hamdu lillah', not the fact that praise belongs to Allah.

After defining proposition types, the author addresses an objection: 'al-hamdu lillah' cannot be a declarative (insha'iyya) sentence because the servant cannot create its content or judgment. The content is explained in detail, and then the answer clarifies that 'insha'iyya' here means creating praise, not the content or judgment. This lesson unpacks the components of a proposition (content and judgment) and shows how the objection is resolved, which is essential for understanding how logicians analyze Islamic utterances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parts of a proposition: content (madhmūn) and judgment (hukm)
The author defines content as the verbal noun extracted from the predicate and attributed to the subject (e.g., 'Zayd's standing' from 'Zayd is standing'). For solid predicates, it is existence attributed to the subject with the predicate as a predicate. Judgment is the affirmation (thubūt) of that content.
Content is what is affirmed, judgment is the affirmation itself.
2
Understand the objection: the servant cannot create the content or judgment
The objector argues that in 'al-hamdu lillah', the content (praise belonging to Allah) and the judgment (that it is established) are eternal truths, not created by the servant's utterance. Therefore, the sentence cannot be insha'iyya (which would create something new).
This objection seems to assume insha'iyya means creating the propositional content or its truth.
3
Analyze the answer: insha'iyya means creating praise (thanā')
The author responds that 'insha'iyya' does not mean creating the content or judgment, but creating the act of praising by means of the utterance. The servant brings about praise through his statement, even though the content and judgment are independent of him.
This shifts the focus from the proposition's truth to the speech act's function.
4
Connect to the broader logical principle: how logicians categorize sentences
This resolution shows that logical analysis distinguishes between the propositional content (what is said) and the illocutionary force (the act performed by saying it). 'Al-hamdu lillah' is both a statement of fact (and therefore can be true/false) and an act of praising (and therefore insha'iyya in a specific sense).
This nuance is important for debates in usul al-fiqh about performative utterances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ لَهُ فِي ضِمْنِ الأَفْرَادِ بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الكُلِّيَّةِ وَالجُزْئِيَّةِ، كَانَتْ «قَضِيَّةٌ مُهْمَلَةٌ». وَلَا مَانِعَ هُنَا مِنْ جَعْلِهَا طَبِيعِيَّة)؛ بِأَنْ تُجْعَلَ أَلْ» فِيهَا لِلجِنْسِ وَالطَّبِيعَةِ، بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الْأَفْرَادِ. وَاسْتُشْكِلَ كَوْنَهَا إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ : بِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ العَبْدَ أَنْ يُنْشِئَ مَضْمُونَ هَذِهِ الجُمْلَةِ وَلَا حُكْمَهَا : - وَالأَوَّلُ هُوَ : اخْتِصَاصُ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالحَمْدِ إِنْ قُدِّرَ الخَبَرُ مِنْ مَادَّةِ الاِخْتِصَاص) أَوِ اسْتِحْقَاقُهُ لَهُ إِنْ قُدْرَ مِنْ مَادَّةِ الاِسْتِحْقَاقِ، أَوْ مُلْكُهُ لَهُ إِنْ قُدِّرَ مِنْ مَادَّةِ المِلْكِ؛ لِأَنَّ مَضْمُونَ الجُمْلَةِ هُوَ المَصْدَرُ المُتَصَيَّدُ مِنَ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ المُضَافُ لِلمَحْكُومٍ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كَانَ المَحْكُومُ بِهِ مُشْتَقًا كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكِ: «زَيْدٌ قَائِمٌ»، أَوِ الكَوْنُ المُضَافُ لِلمَحْكُومٍ عَلَيْهِ مَعْ جَعَلِ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ خَبَراً عَنْ ذَلِكَ الكَوْنِ إِنْ كَانَ المَحْكُومُ بِهِ جَامِداً كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ : زَيْدٌ أَسَدٌ». وَالثَّانِي : ثُبُوتُ مَا ذُكِرَ ; لِأَنَّ حُكْمَ الجُمْلَةِ هُوَ الثُّبُوتُ المُضَافُ لِمَضْمُونِهَا ، وَيُرَادِفُهُ : النِّسْبَةُ، وَالمَعْنَى ، وَالمَفْهُومُ . وَأُجِيْبَ : بِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ المُرَادُ بِـ كَوْنِهَا إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ» : كَوْنَهَا لِإِنْشَاء مَضْمُونَهَا أَوْ حُكْمَهَا، بَلْ كَوْنُهَا لِإِنْشَاءِ الثَّنَاءِ بِذَلِكَ . وَالكَلَامُ عَلَى الحَمْدَلَةِ قَدْ شَاعَ وَذَاعَ، فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى ذِكْرِهِ

Defining the Intellect: A Spiritual Tool for Perception
Definition of intellect as a spiritual light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of the definition of intellect according to Bajuri and distinguish the intellect from the soul.

Core Idea
The intellect is not the perceiver; it is the tool by which the soul perceives.

Bajuri presents the most famous definition of the intellect as a 'spiritual light' by which the soul perceives necessary and theoretical sciences. However, he immediately clarifies a crucial point: the soul is the actual perceiver, and the intellect is merely an instrument. This lesson breaks down that definition and explains why describing the intellect as a perceiver is a concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined (العقل) and the core of the definition: 'نور روحاني' (a spiritual light).
The definition is metaphorical; it compares intellect to light.
2
Extract the function
Notice the phrase 'به تدرك النفس العلوم' (by which the soul perceives the sciences). The function of the intellect is instrumental.
3
Distinguish the agent from the instrument
Bajuri explicitly states that the soul is the perceiver (المدركة) and the intellect is a tool (آلة). This is a key correction to common misconceptions.
This distinction is important for theological debates about human agency.
4
Recognize the metaphorical language
Bajuri notes that describing the intellect as perceiving is a concession (تسمح). Understand why such language is allowed but not technically accurate.
This shows precision in philosophical terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) وَحَطَّ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ سَمَاءِ العَقْلِ كُلَّ حِجَابٍ مِنْ سَحَابِ الجَهْلِ
الباجوري
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي العَقْلِ عَلَى أَقْوَالٍ كَثِيرَةٍ أَشْهَرُهَا - وَهُوَ الأَسْلَمُ - أَنَّهُ : «نُورٌ رُوحَانِيٌّ بِهِ تُدْرِكُ النَّفْسُ العُلُومَ الضَّرُورِيَّةَ وَالنَّظَرِيَّةَ ، فَالنَّفْسُ (۱) هِيَ المُدْرِكَةُ ، وَالعَقْلُ آلَةٌ فِي إِدْرَاكِهَا ؛ كَمَا قَالَهُ المُحَقِّقُونَ، فَمَا يَقَعُ فِي كَثِيرٍ مِنَ العِبَارَاتِ مِنْ وَصْفِهِ بِـ الإِدْرَاكِ»، فَهُوَ عَلَى ضَرْبٍ مِنَ التَّسَمُّحِ.
قَوْلُهُ : (وَحَطَّ ... إلخ) مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : «أَخْرَجَا ... إلخ» ؛ مِنْ عَطْفِ السَّبَبِ عَلَى المُسَبَّبِ، أَوِ المَعْلُولِ
الأنبابي
قوله : (رُوحَانِيُّ) أي : منسوب لـ «الرُّوح»؛ من نسبة الشَّيء إلى ما شابهه، ووجه المشابهة: الخفاء في كل.
قوله : (بِهِ تُدْرِكُ) تقديم الجار والمجرور ؛ للاهتمام بشرف العقل، لا للاختصاص. قوله : (العُلُومَ) المراد بها : «المعلومات»؛ ليصح تسلط الإدراك عليها .
قوله : (الضَّرُورِيَّة) أي: الحاصلة لا عن نظرٍ.
قوله : (وَالنَّظَرِيَّة) أي: الحاصلة عن نظر.
قوله : (فَالنَّفْسُ هِيَ المُدْرِكَةُ، وَالعَقْلُ آلَةٌ فِي إِدْرَاكِهَا وهذا مبنيٌّ على تغاير العقل والنَّفس، وعليه فالنَّفْسُ : مَعْنِّى لَطِيفٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ بِهِ حَيَاةُ الإِنْسَانِ».
وذهب الحكماء إلى اتحادهما، وقسموا النفس أربعة أقسام فقالوا :
(۱) ـ إنَّها في مبدأ الفطرة خالية عن العلوم كلها، لكنَّها مستعدة لها، وإلا لامتنع اتصافها بها، وحينئذ تسمى : عقلاً هَيُوليا»؛ تشبيهاً لها بالهَيُولى الخالية في نفسها عن جميع الصُّور القابلة لها . (۲) - ثمَّ إذا استعملت آلاتها - أعني : الحواس الظاهرة والباطنة ، وحصل لها علوم أوَّليَّة، واستعدت لاكتساب النَّظريَّات سميت بـ: «العقل الفعّال». (۳) - ثمَّ إذا رتَّبت العلوم الأوَّليَّة، وأدركتِ النَّظريَّات مشاهدة لها سمّيت بـ: «العقل المستفاد»؛ لاستفادته مِنَ العقل الفعّال .
( ٤ ) - وإذا صارت مخزونةً عندها، وحصلت لها مَلَكةُ الاستحضار متى شاءت من غير تجشم جديد سميت : «عقلاً بالفعل».
قوله : (مِنْ عَطْفِ السَّبَبِ عَلَى المُسَبَّبِ ) أي : لأنَّ حطّ الحُجُبِ سبب لإخراج النتائج .
(2) And He removed from them from the heaven of intellect every veil of the clouds of ignorance. Al-Bajuri: And know that there is disagreement about the intellect on many opinions, the most famous of which – and it is the safest – is that it is: 'A spiritual light by which the soul perceives the necessary and theoretical sciences. So the soul is the perceiver, and the intellect is a tool in its perception, as the investigators have said. Thus what occurs in many expressions of describing it as having perception is a kind of concession.' His saying 'and He removed...' is coordinated with his saying 'has brought out...' as a conjunction of cause upon effect. Al-Anbābī: His saying 'spiritual' means attributed to 'spirit' (rūḥ) by way of comparison, the similarity being subtlety in everything. His saying 'by it perceives' fronting the prepositional phrase is for emphasizing the honor of the intellect, not for exclusivity. His saying 'the sciences' intends 'the known things' (ma‘lūmāt) so that perception can be applied to them. His saying 'necessary' meaning what is obtained without investigation. His saying 'theoretical' meaning what is obtained by investigation. His saying 'so the soul is the perceiver and the intellect is a tool in its perception' is built on the differentiation between intellect and soul; accordingly, the soul is a subtle spiritual entity by which is the life of man. And the philosophers went to their unity, and divided the soul into four parts, saying: (1) In the beginning of nature it is empty of all sciences, but it is prepared for them – otherwise it would be impossible for it to be characterized by them – and then it is called 'material intellect' (al-‘aql al-hayūlānī) by analogy to prime matter void of all forms receptive to them. (2) Then when it uses its instruments, meaning the external and internal senses, and acquires primary sciences and is prepared to acquire theoretical ones, it is called 'active intellect' (al-‘aql al-fa‘‘āl). (3) Then when it arranges the primary sciences and perceives the theoretical ones as witnessed, it is called 'acquired intellect' (al-‘aql al-mustafād) because it benefits from the active intellect. (4) And when they become stored in it and it acquires the faculty of recollection whenever it wishes without new effort, it is called 'actual intellect' (al-‘aql bi al-fi‘l). His saying 'from conjunction of cause upon effect' means that the removal of veils is the cause for bringing out results.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage defines the intellect according to the author and then details its four stages as per the philosophers. It begins with the second line of the poem: 'And He removed from them from the heaven of intellect every veil of the clouds of ignorance.' Bajuri then presents the most famous definition of intellect: it is a spiritual light by which the soul perceives both necessary and theoretical knowledge. He clarifies that the soul is the actual perceiver while the intellect is merely an instrument, and descriptions of the intellect as perceiving are metaphorical. Al-Anbābī then explains the word 'spiritual' as a relational term to 'spirit' due to subtlety. He also notes that fronting the prepositional phrase 'by it' is for emphasis, not restriction. He clarifies that 'sciences' here means 'known things' so that perception can be properly applied. The distinction between necessary (obtained without investigation) and theoretical (obtained by investigation) knowledge is explained. Bajuri then notes that the philosophers (ḥukamā') consider the soul and intellect to be one and the same, and they divide the soul into four stages: (1) The material intellect (al-‘aql al-hayūlānī) – the soul in its initial state devoid of knowledge but with potential. (2) The active intellect (al-‘aql al-fa‘‘āl) – after acquiring primary sciences through senses and being prepared for theoretical knowledge. (3) The acquired intellect (al-‘aql al-mustafād) – when it organizes primary knowledge and perceives theoretical knowledge directly. (4) The actual intellect (al-‘aql bi al-fi‘l) – when knowledge is stored and can be recalled at will without new effort. Finally, he explains the conjunction of the second line to the first as cause and effect: removing veils causes the bringing out of results.

Key Terms
العقل
النفس
نور روحاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Bajuri, what is the role of the intellect in perception?
A) It is the perceiver of all knowledge.
B) It is a tool used by the soul to perceive.
C) It is the same as the soul.
D) It perceives independently of the soul.

Key Takeaway
The intellect is a spiritual instrument for the soul's perception, not the perceiver itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Soul and Intellect: Unity or Distinction?
Disagreement on soul-intellect relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the theologians' view (that the soul and intellect are distinct) with the philosophers' view (that they are identical) as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Philosophers equate soul and intellect; theologians differentiate them.

Bajuri presents two positions: the preferred view that the soul and intellect are distinct, and the philosophers' view that they are one. He then explains how the philosophers divide the soul into four stages, each called by a different name of the intellect. This lesson explores that disagreement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two positions
Find where Bajuri states the disagreement and the two options: the 'safe' opinion (al-aslam) that they are distinct, and the philosophers' view of unity.
2
Understand the philosophers' position
The philosophers 'went to their unity' (ذهب الحكماء إلى اتحادهما). This is a crucial claim.
This unity means that the intellect is the soul in different states.
3
Trace the implications
If they are one, then the four stages of the soul are also stages of the intellect. The philosophers divide the soul into four intellects.
4
Contrast with the theologians' view
The theologians (mutakallimūn) treat the soul as a separate substance from the intellect, which has implications for eschatology and human identity.
This distinction matters for knowledge of the soul after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) وَحَطَّ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ سَمَاءِ العَقْلِ كُلَّ حِجَابٍ مِنْ سَحَابِ الجَهْلِ
الباجوري
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي العَقْلِ عَلَى أَقْوَالٍ كَثِيرَةٍ أَشْهَرُهَا - وَهُوَ الأَسْلَمُ - أَنَّهُ : «نُورٌ رُوحَانِيٌّ بِهِ تُدْرِكُ النَّفْسُ العُلُومَ الضَّرُورِيَّةَ وَالنَّظَرِيَّةَ ، فَالنَّفْسُ (۱) هِيَ المُدْرِكَةُ ، وَالعَقْلُ آلَةٌ فِي إِدْرَاكِهَا ؛ كَمَا قَالَهُ المُحَقِّقُونَ، فَمَا يَقَعُ فِي كَثِيرٍ مِنَ العِبَارَاتِ مِنْ وَصْفِهِ بِـ الإِدْرَاكِ»، فَهُوَ عَلَى ضَرْبٍ مِنَ التَّسَمُّحِ.
قَوْلُهُ : (وَحَطَّ ... إلخ) مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : «أَخْرَجَا ... إلخ» ؛ مِنْ عَطْفِ السَّبَبِ عَلَى المُسَبَّبِ، أَوِ المَعْلُولِ
الأنبابي
قوله : (رُوحَانِيُّ) أي : منسوب لـ «الرُّوح»؛ من نسبة الشَّيء إلى ما شابهه، ووجه المشابهة: الخفاء في كل.
قوله : (بِهِ تُدْرِكُ) تقديم الجار والمجرور ؛ للاهتمام بشرف العقل، لا للاختصاص. قوله : (العُلُومَ) المراد بها : «المعلومات»؛ ليصح تسلط الإدراك عليها .
قوله : (الضَّرُورِيَّة) أي: الحاصلة لا عن نظرٍ.
قوله : (وَالنَّظَرِيَّة) أي: الحاصلة عن نظر.
قوله : (فَالنَّفْسُ هِيَ المُدْرِكَةُ، وَالعَقْلُ آلَةٌ فِي إِدْرَاكِهَا وهذا مبنيٌّ على تغاير العقل والنَّفس، وعليه فالنَّفْسُ : مَعْنِّى لَطِيفٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ بِهِ حَيَاةُ الإِنْسَانِ».
وذهب الحكماء إلى اتحادهما، وقسموا النفس أربعة أقسام فقالوا :
(۱) ـ إنَّها في مبدأ الفطرة خالية عن العلوم كلها، لكنَّها مستعدة لها، وإلا لامتنع اتصافها بها، وحينئذ تسمى : عقلاً هَيُوليا»؛ تشبيهاً لها بالهَيُولى الخالية في نفسها عن جميع الصُّور القابلة لها . (۲) - ثمَّ إذا استعملت آلاتها - أعني : الحواس الظاهرة والباطنة ، وحصل لها علوم أوَّليَّة، واستعدت لاكتساب النَّظريَّات سميت بـ: «العقل الفعّال». (۳) - ثمَّ إذا رتَّبت العلوم الأوَّليَّة، وأدركتِ النَّظريَّات مشاهدة لها سمّيت بـ: «العقل المستفاد»؛ لاستفادته مِنَ العقل الفعّال .
( ٤ ) - وإذا صارت مخزونةً عندها، وحصلت لها مَلَكةُ الاستحضار متى شاءت من غير تجشم جديد سميت : «عقلاً بالفعل».
قوله : (مِنْ عَطْفِ السَّبَبِ عَلَى المُسَبَّبِ ) أي : لأنَّ حطّ الحُجُبِ سبب لإخراج النتائج .
(2) And He removed from them from the heaven of intellect every veil of the clouds of ignorance. Al-Bajuri: And know that there is disagreement about the intellect on many opinions, the most famous of which – and it is the safest – is that it is: 'A spiritual light by which the soul perceives the necessary and theoretical sciences. So the soul is the perceiver, and the intellect is a tool in its perception, as the investigators have said. Thus what occurs in many expressions of describing it as having perception is a kind of concession.' His saying 'and He removed...' is coordinated with his saying 'has brought out...' as a conjunction of cause upon effect. Al-Anbābī: His saying 'spiritual' means attributed to 'spirit' (rūḥ) by way of comparison, the similarity being subtlety in everything. His saying 'by it perceives' fronting the prepositional phrase is for emphasizing the honor of the intellect, not for exclusivity. His saying 'the sciences' intends 'the known things' (ma‘lūmāt) so that perception can be applied to them. His saying 'necessary' meaning what is obtained without investigation. His saying 'theoretical' meaning what is obtained by investigation. His saying 'so the soul is the perceiver and the intellect is a tool in its perception' is built on the differentiation between intellect and soul; accordingly, the soul is a subtle spiritual entity by which is the life of man. And the philosophers went to their unity, and divided the soul into four parts, saying: (1) In the beginning of nature it is empty of all sciences, but it is prepared for them – otherwise it would be impossible for it to be characterized by them – and then it is called 'material intellect' (al-‘aql al-hayūlānī) by analogy to prime matter void of all forms receptive to them. (2) Then when it uses its instruments, meaning the external and internal senses, and acquires primary sciences and is prepared to acquire theoretical ones, it is called 'active intellect' (al-‘aql al-fa‘‘āl). (3) Then when it arranges the primary sciences and perceives the theoretical ones as witnessed, it is called 'acquired intellect' (al-‘aql al-mustafād) because it benefits from the active intellect. (4) And when they become stored in it and it acquires the faculty of recollection whenever it wishes without new effort, it is called 'actual intellect' (al-‘aql bi al-fi‘l). His saying 'from conjunction of cause upon effect' means that the removal of veils is the cause for bringing out results.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage defines the intellect according to the author and then details its four stages as per the philosophers. It begins with the second line of the poem: 'And He removed from them from the heaven of intellect every veil of the clouds of ignorance.' Bajuri then presents the most famous definition of intellect: it is a spiritual light by which the soul perceives both necessary and theoretical knowledge. He clarifies that the soul is the actual perceiver while the intellect is merely an instrument, and descriptions of the intellect as perceiving are metaphorical. Al-Anbābī then explains the word 'spiritual' as a relational term to 'spirit' due to subtlety. He also notes that fronting the prepositional phrase 'by it' is for emphasis, not restriction. He clarifies that 'sciences' here means 'known things' so that perception can be properly applied. The distinction between necessary (obtained without investigation) and theoretical (obtained by investigation) knowledge is explained. Bajuri then notes that the philosophers (ḥukamā') consider the soul and intellect to be one and the same, and they divide the soul into four stages: (1) The material intellect (al-‘aql al-hayūlānī) – the soul in its initial state devoid of knowledge but with potential. (2) The active intellect (al-‘aql al-fa‘‘āl) – after acquiring primary sciences through senses and being prepared for theoretical knowledge. (3) The acquired intellect (al-‘aql al-mustafād) – when it organizes primary knowledge and perceives theoretical knowledge directly. (4) The actual intellect (al-‘aql bi al-fi‘l) – when knowledge is stored and can be recalled at will without new effort. Finally, he explains the conjunction of the second line to the first as cause and effect: removing veils causes the bringing out of results.

Key Terms
العقل
النفس
اتحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the philosophers' view on the relationship between the soul and the intellect?
A) They are two separate substances.
B) They are identical (اتحاد).
C) The intellect is a part of the soul.
D) The soul is a tool of the intellect.

Key Takeaway
Philosophers identify the soul and intellect, while the preferred view separates them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Compare the two views: (1) The soul is a subtle substance and the intellect is a tool; (2) The soul and intellect are identical. Write one sentence explaining how each view would explain the phenomenon of memory recall.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
5 min
The Four Stages of the Intellect
Four stages of the intellect according to philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate the four stages of the intellect: material, active, acquired, and actual.

Core Idea
The human intellect progresses from pure potentiality to full actuality through four stages.

The philosophers divided the soul's intellectual development into four stages, each with a distinct name. Starting from empty potential (material intellect), through acquiring basic sciences (active intellect), to organizing and directly perceiving theoretical knowledge (acquired intellect), and finally to having knowledge stored and recallable at will (actual intellect). This lesson dissects these stages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four stages in order
Scan the passage for the four names: العقل الهيولاني, العقل الفعّال, العقل المستفاد, عقلاً بالفعل. Note the Arabic sequence.
The stages correspond to increasing actualization.
2
Understand the material intellect
The first stage is like prime matter: empty but ready to receive. The text uses the analogy of prime matter (هيولى).
This is the intellect in potentiality.
3
Understand the progression
Each stage builds on the previous: from primary sciences to theoretical knowledge to storage and recall.
The active intellect here is not the cosmic intellect but a stage of the human soul.
4
Differentiate the acquired and actual intellects
The acquired intellect is when theoretical knowledge is perceived directly (مشاهدة), while actual intellect is when knowledge is stored and recallable.
This distinction is subtle but important for understanding different levels of knowledge.

What Is Mantiq?

The Intellect as a Spiritual Light
Author defines 'aql as a spiritual light and distinguishes perceiver from instrument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct definition of the intellect in Islamic logic and distinguish between the soul's perception and the intellect's instrumental role.

Core Idea
The intellect is not the perceiver; it is the instrument by which the soul perceives.

In this lesson, we examine the most famous definition of the intellect ('aql) in the Islamic logical tradition. The author presents it as a 'spiritual light' but carefully explains that perception belongs to the soul, not the intellect itself. This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definiendum and the definition
Identify the term being defined: العقل (al-'aql). The definition given is 'نور روحاني' (a spiritual light).
2
Identify the function of the intellect
The intellect is that 'به تدرك النفس العلوم الضرورية والنظرية' (by which the soul perceives necessary and theoretical sciences). Note the role: the soul perceives, the intellect enables.
3
Distinguish soul and intellect
The text explicitly states 'النفس هي المدركة والعقل آلة في إدراكها' (the soul is the perceiver, and the intellect is an instrument in its perception). Observe that the soul is the subject, the intellect is the tool.
4
Recognize metaphorical license
The author notes that describing the intellect itself as 'perceiving' is a form of التسمح (metaphorical license). Understand that such expressions are not literal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي العَقْلِ عَلَى أَقْوَالٍ كَثِيرَةٍ أَشْهَرُهَا - وَهُوَ الأَسْلَمُ - أَنَّهُ : «نُورٌ رُوحَانِيٌّ بِهِ تُدْرِكُ النَّفْسُ العُلُومَ الضَّرُورِيَّةَ وَالنَّظَرِيَّةَ ، فَالنَّفْسُ هِيَ المُدْرِكَةُ ، وَالعَقْلُ آلَةٌ فِي إِدْرَاكِهَا ؛ كَمَا قَالَهُ المُحَقِّقُونَ، فَمَا يَقَعُ فِي كَثِيرٍ مِنَ العِبَارَاتِ مِنْ وَصْفِهِ بِـ الإِدْرَاكِ»، فَهُوَ عَلَى ضَرْبٍ مِنَ التَّسَمُّحِ.
And know that there is disagreement about the intellect on many opinions, the most famous of which—and it is the safest—is that it is: 'A spiritual light by which the soul perceives necessary and theoretical sciences. So the soul is the perceiver, and the intellect is an instrument in its perception, as the verifiers have said. So what occurs in many expressions of describing it with perception is a kind of metaphorical license.'
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage defines the intellect ('aql) as a spiritual light (nur ruhani). It clarifies that the soul (nafs) is the actual perceiver, while the intellect serves as an instrument for perception. The author warns that describing the intellect itself as 'perceiving' is a form of metaphorical license (tassamuh), not to be taken literally. This is a foundational definition in Islamic logic, establishing the epistemological role of the intellect as a tool for acquiring knowledge.

Key Terms
العقل
النور الروحاني
الإدراك
التسمح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most famous opinion cited, what is the intellect's role in perception?
A) The intellect perceives directly.
B) The intellect is an instrument for the soul's perception.
C) The intellect creates knowledge.
D) The intellect is identical to the soul.

Key Takeaway
The intellect is defined as a spiritual light through which the soul perceives, and it is an instrument, not the perceiver itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Distinguishing Mafhum and Masdaq of Iman and Islam
Bajuri explains why the matn mentions both iman and islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the concepts (mafhum) and referents (masdaq) of 'iman' and 'islam' and explain why they are mentioned separately despite their inseparable coexistence.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam differ in definition and in the acts they denote, yet every believer is simultaneously a Muslim.

Why does the author of the matn mention both 'iman' and 'islam' when they always go together in a believer? Al-Bajuri answers that although they are inseparable in existence (talazum), they differ in concept (mafhum) and referent (masdaq). This lesson unpacks that logical distinction and shows how two terms can be co-extensive yet have different meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the puzzle
Notice the matn mentions both 'iman' and 'islam' despite their inseparable coexistence. Al-Bajuri explicitly states that they necessarily entail each other: wherever iman exists, islam exists and vice versa.
Separation in mention does not imply separation in existence.
2
Differentiate concept (mafhum) from referent (masdaq)
Mafhum is the meaning or definition of a term; masdaq is the set of external instances that fall under it. The passage argues that iman and islam differ in both. First, examine their conceptual definitions (linguistic and legal).
This distinction is foundational in logic and usul al-fiqh.
3
Extract the definitions
From the passage: iman linguistically = absolute tasdiq; legally = tasdiq and iqrar with what the Prophet brought from what is known by necessity. Islam linguistically = absolute inqiyad; legally = inqiyad to what the Prophet brought, meaning compliance such that if commanded one obeys.
Tasdiq and inqiyad are different concepts.
4
Compare the referents
The referents of iman are individual acts of tasdiq (Zayd's tasdiq, Amr's tasdiq, etc.); the referents of islam are individual acts of inqiyad (Zayd's inqiyad, Amr's inqiyad, etc.). Thus the two terms pick out different classes of actions.
Yet each person has both types of acts—hence unity of locus.
5
Note the co-extensiveness
Despite different concepts and different referential classes, iman and islam are 'united in locus' (muttahidan mahalla). Every place where an act of tasdiq occurs, an act of inqiyad also occurs in the same person, and vice versa. This is their inseparable coexistence.
Complete iman is always accompanied by complete islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا جَمَعَ المُصَنِّفُ بَيْنَ الإِيْمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ مَعَ تَلَازُمِهِمَا وُجُوداً - بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ مِنْ وُجُودِ الإِيمَانِ فِي شَخْصٍ وُجُودُ الإِسْلَامِ فِيهِ، وَبِالعَكْسِ ؛ لِتَغَابِرِهِمَا مَنْهُوماً وَمَا صَدَقاً : أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ، فَلِأَنَّ : مَنْهُومَ الإِيمَانِ لُغَةٌ : مُطْلَقُ التَصْدِيقِ، وَمِنْهُ : ﴿وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُؤْمِنٍ لَّنَا﴾ [يوسف: ١٧] . وَشَرْعاً : التَّصْدِيقُ وَالإِنْعَانُ بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ الله مِمَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدِّيْنِ بِالضَّرُورَةِ. وَمَنْهُومُ الإِسْلَامِ لُغَةٌ: «مُطْلَقُ الإِنْقِيَادِ». وَشَرْعاً : الإِنْقِيَادُ لِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَذَلِكَ ، وَالمُرَادُ بِـ «الإِنْقِيَادِ لِذَلِكَ : الِامْتِثَالُ لَهُ بِحَيْثُ لَوْ أُمِرَ لَأَتَمَرَ. وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي، فَلِأَنَّ مَاصَدُقَاتِ الإِيمَانِ تَصْدِيقَاتٌ كَـ: «تَصْدِيقِ زَيْدٍ، وَتَصْدِيقِ عَمْرٍو، وَتَصْدِيقِ بَكْرٍ، وَهَكَذَا، وَمَاصَدُقَاتِ الإِسْلَامِ انْقِيَادَاتٌ كَـ: انْقِيَادِ زَيْدٍ، وَانْقِيَادِ عَمْرٍو، وَانْقِيَادِ بَكْرٍ، ... وَهَكَذَا». نَعَمْ؛ هُمَا مُتَّحِدَانِ مَحَلَّا؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّ كُلَّ مَحَلٌّ لِلإِيمَانِ مَحَلٌّ لِلإِسْلَامِ وَعَكْسُهُ؛ لِتَلَازُمِهِمَا وُجُوداً كَمَا عَلِمْتَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ المُرَادُ مِنِ اتَّحَادِهِمَا مَاصَدَقَا فِي عِبَارَةِ مَنْ عَبَّرَ بِهِ. وَالكَلَامُ فِي الإِيمَانِ الكَامِلِ بِمُصَاحَبَةِ الإِسْلَامِ، وَفِي الإِسْلَامِ الكَامِلِ بِمُصَاحَبَةِ الإِيمَانِ.
And the author only combined between iman and islam despite their mutual coexistence in existence — meaning that from the existence of iman in a person, the existence of islam in him necessarily follows, and vice versa — because they differ in concept and referent. As for the first [concept], it is because: the concept of iman linguistically is absolute tasdiq, and from that is [the verse] 'And you are not a believer for us' [Yusuf: 17]. And legally: tasdiq and iqrar with what the Prophet brought, from what is known of the religion by necessity. And the concept of islam linguistically is absolute inqiyad. And legally: inqiyad to what the Prophet brought similarly, and the intended meaning of inqiyad to that is compliance with him such that if commanded he would obey. And as for the second [referent], it is because the referents of iman are tasdiq acts, like Zayd's tasdiq, Amr's tasdiq, Bakr's tasdiq, and so on. And the referents of islam are inqiyad acts, like Zayd's inqiyad, Amr's inqiyad, Bakr's inqiyad, and so on. Yes, they are united in locus, meaning every place of iman is a place of islam and vice versa, due to their mutual coexistence in existence as you have learned, and this is the intended meaning of their unity in referent in the expression of whoever expressed it. And the discussion is about complete iman accompanied by islam, and about complete islam accompanied by iman.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage expands on why the author of the matn mentions both 'iman' and 'islam' even though they necessarily coexist in any individual. The commentator, al-Bajuri, explains that while they are inseparable in existence, they differ conceptually and referentially. He first notes that iman and islam are mutually entailing: if a person has iman, they necessarily have islam, and vice versa. Despite this, they are distinct in meaning (concept) and in individual instances (referents). To demonstrate the conceptual difference, he provides linguistic and legal definitions: linguistically, iman is 'absolute tasdiq' (affirmation) and legally it is 'tasdiq and iqrar with what the Prophet brought from what is known by necessity'; linguistically, islam is 'absolute inqiyad' (submission) and legally it is 'inqiyad to what the Prophet brought' meaning compliance such that if commanded one would obey. These definitions show two different meanings (tasdiq vs. inqiyad). Then he shows that their referents are also different: the referents of iman are individual acts of tasdiq (like Zayd's tasdiq), while the referents of islam are individual acts of inqiyad (like Zayd's inqiyad). Thus the two terms pick out different sets of particular acts. Nevertheless, he clarifies that they are 'united in locus' meaning that wherever there is an act of tasdiq there is also an act of inqiyad in the same person, and vice versa. This unity is due to their necessary co-existence. The discussion is about complete iman and complete islam, each accompanied by the other. The key logical point is that two terms can have different definitions (intensions) and refer to different classes of particulars (extensions) yet be co-extensive in terms of the persons who possess them.

الإسلام
مفهوم
ماصدق

Checkpoint
According to Bajuri's commentary, what is the relationship between the concepts of 'iman' and 'islam'?
A) They are identical in meaning and referent.
B) They differ in meaning but share the same referent in the person.
C) They differ in referent but share the same meaning.
D) They are unrelated in meaning and referent.

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are two different concepts (tasdiq vs inqiyad) with different referents (acts of affirming vs acts of submitting), yet they are inseparable in every believing person.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the same pattern as al-Bajuri, write a short passage distinguishing the concept (mafhum) and referent (masdaq) of 'salat' (linguistic: du'a; legal: specific acts). Illustrate how they differ in meaning but can be co-extensive in certain contexts.
?
Find a fiqh text where two terms (e.g., 'gunah' and 'ithm') are used. Analyze whether they differ in concept or referent using the mafhum/masdaq framework from this lesson.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
10 min
Definitions of Iman and Islam and Their Logical Relationship
Bajuri defines Iman and Islam and explains their logical entailment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conceptual definitions (mafhum) of Iman and Islam from their extensions (masadiq), and identify when they are necessarily co-extensive and when they are not.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are distinct in concept but co-extensive in their complete forms yet separable in their basics.

In this passage, Bajuri defines two foundational terms of our religion: Iman and Islam. He not only gives their legal definitions but also clarifies a subtle logical relationship: while they differ in meaning, their complete forms always coexist. This distinction between concept and instance is a key logical tool you will use in many Islamic sciences, especially in Usul al-Fiqh and Kalam, where precision about terms prevents wrong conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Extract the legal definitions
Identify the legal (shar‘i) definitions of Iman and Islam from the passage. Iman is defined as 'tasdiq' (confirmation) and 'idhan' (submission) to what the Prophet brought. Islam is defined as 'inqiyad' (submission/compliance) to what the Prophet brought, explained as immediate obedience if commanded.
Note that the definitions include both inner and outer aspects, but the emphasis differs: Iman highlights inner confirmation, Islam highlights outer submission.
2
Distinguish between concept (mafhum) and instance (masdaq)
The passage introduces the logical distinction between mafhum (the conceptual meaning) and masdaq (the actual individuals that fall under the concept). Bajuri points out that the concepts of Iman and Islam are different, but their instances (e.g., Zayd's confirmation vs. Zayd's submission) are considered in relation.
This distinction is crucial: two concepts may have different meanings yet apply to the same individuals in reality.
3
Understand the mutual entailment (talazum) of the complete forms
Bajuri states that every locus of complete Iman is a locus of complete Islam and vice versa. This is because complete Iman necessarily requires complete submission, and complete submission necessarily requires inner confirmation. They are mutually entailed in existence.
The word 'complete' is key: the author is not talking about the bare minimum but about fully developed Iman and Islam.
4
Identify the exception for the basic origins
Bajuri clarifies that the basic origins (asl) of Iman and Islam can exist separately. One can have faith in the heart without submitting outwardly, and one can outwardly comply without inner faith. Thus, the mutual entailment only holds for the complete forms, not for the minimal levels.
This nuance is important in fiqh rulings about who is considered a believer or Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَحْمَدُهُ جَلَّ عَلَى الإِنْعَامِ بِنِعْمَةِ الإِيمَانِ وَالإِسْلَامِ

وَشَرْعاً : التَّصْدِيقُ وَالإِذْعَانُ بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِمَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدِّيْنِ بِالضَّرُورَةِ. وَمَنْهُومُ الإِسْلَامِ لُغَةً: مُطْلَقُ الإِنْقِيَادِ. وَشَرْعاً : الإِنْقِيَادُ لِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَذَلِكَ، وَالمُرَادُ بِـ «الإِنْقِيَادِ لِذَلِكَ : الِامْتِثَالُ لَهُ بِحَيْثُ لَوْ أُمِرَ لَائْتَمَرَ. وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي، فَلِأَنَّ مَاصَدَ قَاتِ الإِيمَانِ تَصْدِيقَاتٌ كَـ: تَصْدِيقِ زَيْدٍ، وَتَصْدِيقِ عَمْرٍو، وَتَصْدِيقِ بَكْرٍ، وَهَكَذَا، وَمَاصَدَقَاتِ الإِسْلَامِ انْقِيَادَاتٌ كَـ: انْقِيَادِ زَيْدٍ، وَانْقِيَادِ عَمْرٍو، وَانْقِيَادِ بَكْرٍ، وَهَكَذَا. نَعَمْ؛ هُمَا مُتَّحِدَانِ مَحَلَّا، بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ كُلَّ مَحَلٍّ لِلإِيمَانِ مَحَلٌّ لِلإِسْلَامِ وَعَكْسُهُ، لِتَلَازُمِهِمَا وُجُوداً كَمَا عَلِمْتَ، وَهَذَا هُوَ المُرَادُ مِنِ اتِّحَادِهِمَا مَاصَدَقَا فِي عِبَارَةِ مَنْ عَبَّرَ بِهِ. وَالكَلَامُ فِي الإِيمَانِ الكَامِلِ بِمُصَاحَبَةِ الإِسْلَامِ، وَفِي الإِسْلَامِ الكَامِلِ بِمُصَاحَبَةِ الإِيمَانِ. وَإِلَّا فَأَصْلُ الإِيمَانِ وَأَصْلُ الإِسْلَامِ لَا تَلَازُمَ بَيْنَهُمَا وُجُوداً حَتَّى يَتَّحِدَا مَحَلَّا، بَلْ قَدْ يَنْفَرِدُ الإِيمَانُ كَمَا فِي المُصَدِّقِ بِقَلْبِهِ غَيْرِ المُنْقَادِ، وَقَدْ يَنْفَرِدُ الإِسْلَامُ كَمَا فِي المُنْقَادِ غَيْرِ المُصَدِّقِ بِقَلْبِهِ. وَلَمَّا كَانَتْ نِعْمَةُ الإِيمَانِ وَنِعْمَةُ الإِسْلَامِ أَجَلَّ النِّعَمِ وَأَسَاسَهَا، خَصَّهَا المُصَنِّفُ بِالذِّكْرِ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ نِعَمُ اللهِ تَعَالَى كَثِيرَةً لَا تُحْصَى؛ قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا﴾ [النحل: ١٨].
We praise Him, the Majestic, for the favor of Iman and Islam. And legally: [Iman is] confirmation and submission to what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought, from what is known of the religion by necessity. And the literal meaning of Islam is absolute submission. And legally: submission to what the Prophet, peace be upon him, brought likewise, and what is meant by 'submission to that' is compliance with him such that if he commands, he obeys. As for the second, [it is] because the instances of Iman are confirmations, like the confirmation of Zayd, the confirmation of 'Amr, the confirmation of Bakr, and so on, and the instances of Islam are submissions, like the submission of Zayd, the submission of 'Amr, the submission of Bakr, and so on. Yes, they are unified in locus, meaning that every locus of Iman is a locus of Islam and vice versa, due to their mutual entailment in existence as you have learned, and this is the intended meaning of their unification in instances in the expression of one who expressed it. And the discussion is about complete Iman accompanied by Islam, and about complete Islam accompanied by Iman. Otherwise, the origin of Iman and the origin of Islam have no mutual entailment in existence such that they would be unified in locus; rather, Iman may be separate as in one who confirms with his heart without submitting, and Islam may be separate as in one who submits without confirming with his heart. And since the favor of Iman and the favor of Islam are the greatest favors and their foundation, the author specifically mentioned them, even though the favors of Allah, the Exalted, are many and cannot be counted; Allah, the Exalted, said: 'And if you count the favors of Allah, you cannot enumerate them' [an-Nahl 16:18].
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and dialectical commentary on the matn line praising Allah for the favors of Iman and Islam. The author, Bajuri, begins by providing legal definitions for both terms. Iman is defined as 'tasdiq' (confirmation) and 'idhan' (submission) to what the Prophet brought, specifically that which is known by necessity from the religion. Islam is defined as 'inqiyad' (submission) to what the Prophet brought, and 'inqiyad' is explained as compliance that would result in immediate obedience if commanded. The author then addresses a potential objection: if Iman and Islam are not identical in concept (mafhum), are they at least identical in extension (masadiq)? He clarifies that their complete forms are necessarily co-extensive because any person with complete Iman will also have complete Islam, and vice versa. However, their basic origins can exist independently: one can have bare faith without outward submission, and one can outwardly submit without faith. This distinction is crucial in kalam and fiqh discussions. The passage concludes by noting that these two favors are the greatest, which is why the poet specifically mentioned them in praise.

الإسلام
التصديق
الإذعان
الانقياد
التلازم
المحل
الماصدق

A) They are always co-extensive, because they are the same thing.
B) Only when both are taken in their complete (kamil) forms.
C) Only when the person is a perfect Muslim.
D) They are never co-extensive; they always differ.

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are distinct in concept but their complete forms always coexist, while their basic origins can exist independently.

What Is Mantiq?

Understanding the Grammatical and Rhetorical Depth of a Poetic Blessing
Grammatical and rhetorical analysis of a poetic line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the grammatical function of 'ma' in 'ma dama' and explain the mental metaphor (majaz 'aqli) in the line, using examples from Arabic poetry and tafsir.

Core Idea
A poetic blessing uses grammar and rhetoric to express eternal prayer.

This lesson unpacks a single line of poetry that praises the Prophet with a blessing that seems time‑bound but actually intends perpetuity. The commentator analyzes each word to show how Arab rhetorical conventions work. By learning this, you will see how careful grammatical analysis (i‘rab) and rhetorical awareness (balaghah) are essential for correctly understanding sacred texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle 'ma'
Locate 'ma' in the phrase 'ma dama'. The commentator calls it 'masdariyya' – a verbal noun particle that turns the following clause into a verbal noun. Note that it is also 'zarfiyya' (adverbial), so the phrase means 'for the duration of...'
In Arabic grammar, 'ma dama' is a specific construction of duration.
2
Understand the intended meaning of 'duration'
The commentator emphasizes that the blessing is not literally limited to the time described. Arab custom uses such expressions to convey permanence and eternity. Recognize that the apparent restriction is rhetorical, not literal.
This is a key principle for interpreting oaths and prayers in Islamic texts.
3
Define the term 'al-hija'
The commentator states 'al-hija' means 'al-‘aql' (the intellect). Confirm it is written with kasr and qasr. This word occurs in many classical texts; here it is the intellect that 'plunges' into the sea of meanings.
Be aware of homonyms – in other contexts 'hija' can mean shyness.
4
Identify the mental metaphor (majaz 'aqli)
The verb 'yakhud' (plunges) is attributed to 'al-hija' (intellect). The commentator says this is a mental metaphor because the real agent of plunging is a person, not the intellect. The intellect is figuratively described as plunging into deep meanings.
Mental metaphor is a standard topic in balaghah; it ascribes an action to something indirectly responsible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (مَا دَامَ ... إلخ) «مَا مَصْدَرِيَّةٌ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهَا آلَةٌ فِي سَبْكِ مَا بَعْدَهَا بِمَصْدَرٍ، ظَرْفِيَّةٌ، فَلِذَلِكَ فُسِّرَتْ بـ : «مُدَّةٍ» ، فَالمَعْنَى : «مُدَّةَ دَوَامَ ... إلخ»، وَلَيْسَ المُرَادُ تَقِيدَ الصَّلَاةِ بِهَذِهِ المُدَّةِ، بَلِ المُرَادُ تَابِيدُهَا ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ : صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ اللهُ دَائِماً وَأَبَداً ؛ جَرْياً عَلَى مَا هُوَ عَادَةُ العَرَبِ مِنْ ذِكْرِهِمْ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ، وَيُرِيدُونَ التَّأْبِيدَ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (الحِجَا) هُوَ - بِالكَسْرِ وَالقَصْرِ - : العَقْلُ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ . قَوْلُهُ : ( يَخُوضُ فِيهِ مَجَازٌ عَقْلِيٌّ ؛ لأَنَّ فِيهِ إِسْنَادُ الشَّيْء لِغَيْرِ مَنْ هُوَ لَهُ،
His saying: (ما دام ... etc.). The 'ma' is a masdariyya verbal noun particle meaning it is an instrument for casting what follows into a masdar, adverbial, so for that reason it was explained as 'mudda' (duration), so the meaning is 'duration of continuity ... etc.' Not intending to restrict the blessing to this duration, but rather intending permanence, as if he said: 'May Allah bless him always and forever,' following the customary practice of the Arabs that when they mention such expressions they intend perpetuity. And his saying: (الحجا) it is, with kasr and qasr, the intellect, as previously stated. His saying: (يخوض) in it is a mental metaphor, because it ascribes something to other than whom it belongs to.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the poetic line 'صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ اللهُ مَا دَامَ الحِجَا يَخُوضُ مِنْ بَحْرِ المَعَانِي لُجَجَا'. The commentator explains each word. First, 'ما' is identified as a masdariyya (verbal noun) particle that makes what follows into a verbal noun, and it is adverbial (zarfiyya), so it is interpreted as 'mudda' (duration) meaning 'for the duration of the continuity of...' But the intent is not to restrict the blessing to that specific time, but rather to express perpetuity, as Arab custom uses such expressions to mean eternity. Then 'الحجا' is defined as 'al-ʿaql' (intellect) with kasr of the ha and qasr (shortening). Finally, 'يخوض' is analyzed as a mental metaphor (majaz 'aqli) because the act of 'plunging' is not literally done by the intellect; rather, it is attributed to it figuratively.

Key Terms
ما
الحجا
مجاز عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the phrase 'ما دام' (ma dama) in the line intend?
A) A specific duration
B) Perpetuity
C) The act of plunging
D) The sea of meanings

Key Takeaway
A single poetic line can contain deep grammatical and rhetorical layers; careful analysis reveals that apparent temporal restrictions may actually express permanence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Find a Quranic verse that uses 'ma dama' or a similar construction (e.g., 6:79 'إِنِّي وَجَّهْتُ وَجْهِيَ لِلَّذِي فَطَرَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ حَنِيفًا ۖ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ'). Determine whether the 'ma' is masdariyya or not and explain how the meaning changes.

What Is Mantiq?
