(٤) - وَفَضْلُهُ : فَوَقَانُهُ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ مِنَ العُلُومِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ عَامَّ النَّفْعِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِيُّ (٢) ، وَهَذَا لَا يُنَافِي أَنَّ بَعْضَ بَاقِي العُلُومِ يَفُوقَهُ مِنْ حَيثَيَّةٍ أُخْرَى . الأنبابي (۲) . إلى المجهولات، وما يتوقَّفُ عليه هذا الإيصال، وهذه الأحوال هي العارضة للمعلومات التصورية والتصديقيَّة لذواتها، والفرق بين العوارض الذاتية وغيرها مذكور في القطب» و «حواشيه مع زياداتٍ أُخر متعلقة بالحد والموضوع المذكورين (۳). قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : فموضوع المنطق مقيَّد بصحة الإيصال، لا بنفس الإيصال؛ حتّى يرد عليه : أنَّ قيد الموضوع من تتمته، لا يُبحث عنه في العِلم ؛ إذ لا بدَّ في كلِّ علم من كون موضوعه مسلّم الثبوت، والإيصال مبحوث عنه في هذا العلم، فيجب أن يكون حالاً عارضةً للموضوع، لا مسلَّم الثبوت . ومحصّل الجواب : أنَّ قيد الموضوع هو صحة الإيصال، لا الإيصال نفسه، وعلى هذا القياس نظائر هذا القيد في موضوعات العلوم. قوله : (وَقِيلَ : مَعْرِفَةُ التَّالِيفَاتِ... إلخ) في الحقيقة الثَّمرة الأولى متفرعة على هذه الثَّمرة . (۱) الشرشيمي: قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : المبحوث عنها من حيث صحة الإيصال، لا من حيث ذاتها، وكذلك ومِن حيث ما يتوقف عليه التّوصُّل، أو المعلومات كما تقدَّم، ولعله تركه لعلمه ممَّا سبق، أو اقتصاراً على المقصود. (۲) الشرشيمي: قوله : ( يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي) إن قلت : أيُّ علم تصوري؛ لأنَّ جميع العلوم تصديقات؟ : كل علم فيه تصور وتصديق، فإنَّ علم التوحيد مثلاً إذا قيل فيه: «القُدْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلهِ تَعَالَى، كان إدراك الطرفين تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع النسبة تصديقاً. قلت : ثمَّ ظهر أنَّ المراد بـ التَّصور» في العلوم: تصور تعاريف المفردات منها ؛ كـ تصور معنى الصَّلاة، والبيع، ... إلخ [1/ ١٤]، فإنَّ تعاريفها معلومات تصوريَّة توصل إلى أمر مجهول تصوري، وهو المعرّف، وأنَّ المراد بـ «التصديق» فيها : التصديق بالأقيسة الواقعة فيها ؛ كالقياس الحاصل في مقام الاستدلال على وجوب الصَّلاة بـ (أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ ، فإنَّه يُقال : هذا أمر، وكلُّ أمرٍ للوجوب، وهكذا يقال في سائر الأدلة، وأما نفس الأحكام الفقهية كـ : كون فروض الوضوء ستَّة، أو كونه فرضاً، أو مندوباً ، فلا يُقال لها : معلومات تصوريَّة أو تصديقيَّة توصل ... إلخ» ؛ لأنَّها نفس المصدق بـ به، فهي نتيجة القياس والدليل، وإن كان إدراك مفرداتها تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع نسبتها تصديقاً؛ تأمل. What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
6 min
Concepts and Assent: The Two Types of Knowledge
Commentary distinguishes tasawwur and tasdiq in sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent) as defined in the commentary, and identify examples of each from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
All knowledge is either conception of meanings or assent to judgments.

The passage introduces a crucial distinction that underlies all logical study: the difference between grasping a concept (tasawwur) and affirming or denying a proposition (tasdiq). The commentary, especially from Al-Shirshimi, clarifies how this applies in actual Islamic sciences: conception involves understanding definitions of terms like 'prayer' or 'sale', while assent involves accepting syllogistic proofs that derive rulings. This lesson unpacks that distinction with concrete fiqh examples.

Guided Path
1
Define tasawwur and tasdiq from the text
Find in the commentary where Al-Shirshimi explains: conception is the perception of the two terms; assent is the perception of the occurrence of the relation. Write these definitions in your own words.
Example from tawhid: 'Power is obligatory for Allah' – knowing 'power' and 'obligatory' is conception; affirming the relation is assent.
2
Apply to a fiqh term
Take the term 'prayer' (salat). In fiqh, what does it mean to have tasawwur of prayer? What would be a tasdiq about prayer? Use the commentary's examples.
Tasawwur of prayer is knowing its definition; tasdiq is judging 'prayer is obligatory'.
3
Distinguish premises from conclusions
Al-Shirshimi says actual juristic rulings (e.g., the obligatory acts of ablution are six) are not themselves informational premises but results of reasoning. Identify what is a premise (definition, command) and what is a conclusion (ruling).
This shows logic's role in deriving rulings, not just stating them.

(۱) الشرشيمي: قوله : (مِنْ حَيْثُ صِحَّةِ إِبْصَالِهَا ... إلخ) أي : المبحوث عنها من حيث صحة الإيصال، لا من حيث ذاتها، وكذلك ومِن حيث ما يتوقف عليه التّوصُّل، أو المعلومات كما تقدَّم، ولعله تركه لعلمه ممَّا سبق، أو اقتصاراً على المقصود. (۲) الشرشيمي: قوله : ( يَبْحَثُ عَنْ كُلِّ عِلْمٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِي) إن قلت : أيُّ علم تصوري؛ لأنَّ جميع العلوم تصديقات؟ : كل علم فيه تصور وتصديق، فإنَّ علم التوحيد مثلاً إذا قيل فيه: «القُدْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ لِلهِ تَعَالَى، كان إدراك الطرفين تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع النسبة تصديقاً. قلت : ثمَّ ظهر أنَّ المراد بـ التَّصور» في العلوم: تصور تعاريف المفردات منها ؛ كـ تصور معنى الصَّلاة، والبيع، ... إلخ [1/ ١٤]، فإنَّ تعاريفها معلومات تصوريَّة توصل إلى أمر مجهول تصوري، وهو المعرّف، وأنَّ المراد بـ «التصديق» فيها : التصديق بالأقيسة الواقعة فيها ؛ كالقياس الحاصل في مقام الاستدلال على وجوب الصَّلاة بـ (أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ ، فإنَّه يُقال : هذا أمر، وكلُّ أمرٍ للوجوب، وهكذا يقال في سائر الأدلة، وأما نفس الأحكام الفقهية كـ : كون فروض الوضوء ستَّة، أو كونه فرضاً، أو مندوباً ، فلا يُقال لها : معلومات تصوريَّة أو تصديقيَّة توصل ... إلخ» ؛ لأنَّها نفس المصدق بـ به، فهي نتيجة القياس والدليل، وإن كان إدراك مفرداتها تصوراً، وإدراك وقوع نسبتها تصديقاً؛ تأمل. (۳) انظر: مجموعة الشمسية) (١٥١/١) وما بعدها .
(9) After this: the relation of logic to the mind is like that of grammar to the tongue. Al-Bajuri: (1) From the aspect of the correctness of leading them to an unknown matter, conceptual or assensual. (3) And its fruit: what the author indicated: that it safeguards the mind from error in thinking. And it is said: knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions. (4) And its virtue: its superiority over other sciences by virtue of its general benefit; because it investigates every science, conceptual or assensual. And this does not contradict that some other sciences surpass it from another aspect. Al-Anbabi: (2) ... to the unknowns, and what this leading depends on, and these states are the accidents of conceptual and assensual information in themselves, and the difference between essential accidents and others is mentioned in 'al-Qutb' and its glosses with other additions related to the mentioned definition and subject. His words: 'From the aspect of the correctness of leading them ... etc.' meaning: the subject of logic is restricted to the correctness of leading, not the leading itself; such that it could be objected: the restriction of the subject is part of its completion, it is not investigated in the science; for in every science its subject must be conceded existence, and leading is investigated in this science, so it must be an accidental state of the subject, not conceded existence. The summary of the answer: the restriction of the subject is the correctness of leading, not the leading itself, and on this analogy are similar restrictions in the subjects of sciences. His words: 'And it is said: knowledge of compositions ... etc.' In reality the first fruit branches from this fruit. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'From the aspect of the correctness of leading them ... etc.' meaning: that which is investigated from the aspect of the correctness of leading, not from the aspect of its essence, and likewise from the aspect of what the attainment depends on, or the information as previously mentioned, and perhaps he left it due to knowledge from what preceded, or out of limitation to the intended. (2) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'He investigates every science, conceptual or assensual.' If you say: What science is conceptual? For all sciences are assensuals? (Answer): Every science contains conception and assent, for the science of tawhid, for example, when it is said 'Power is obligatory for Allah the Exalted', the perception of the two terms is conception, and the perception of the occurrence of the relation is assent. I say: Then it became apparent that the intended meaning of 'conception' in the sciences is the conception of the definitions of the individual terms thereof; like the conception of the meaning of prayer, sale, etc., for their definitions are conceptual information leading to an unknown conceptual matter, which is the defined. And that the intended meaning of 'assent' therein is assent to the syllogisms occurring therein; like the syllogism obtained in the context of inference for the obligation of prayer by 'Establish prayer', for it is said: This is a command, and every command is for obligation, and similarly in other evidences. As for the actual juristic rulings, like the obligatory acts of ablution being six, or it being obligatory, or recommended, they are not called conceptual or assensual information leading ... etc., because they are the very things assented to, so they are the result of the syllogism and evidence, although perceiving their terms is conception and perceiving the occurrence of their relation is assent; consider. (3) See: Majmu'a al-Shamsiyya (1/151) and after.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage defines the science of logic (al-mantiq) and explains its fruit (thamara) and virtue (fadl). The opening line draws an analogy: logic relates to the mind as grammar relates to the tongue. Just as grammar preserves the tongue from error in speech, logic preserves the mind from error in thinking (fikr). The author then clarifies that the subject matter of logic is 'information from the aspect of the correctness of leading to an unknown matter' — meaning logic studies the rules that ensure sound inference, whether the unknown is a concept (tasawwur) or a judgment (tasdiq). The fruit of logic is that it safeguards the mind from error in thought, or alternatively, it is the knowledge of correct and corrupt compositions (syllogisms). This is the immediate benefit. The virtue of logic is its generality: it benefits all sciences because it investigates the forms of reasoning used in every discipline. However, this does not mean logic is the noblest science in every respect; other sciences may surpass it in other aspects, such as subject matter or goal. The commentary by al-Anbabi elaborates on the definition: the subject of logic is the 'states' (ahwal) that are accidents of information, specifically essential accidents. He defends the qualification 'correctness of leading' — the subject is not the act of leading itself (which would require prior existence), but the correctness condition. Al-Shirshimi further clarifies that 'conception' in sciences refers to grasping definitions of terms (e.g., the definition of prayer or sale), while 'assent' refers to accepting syllogistic proofs (e.g., deducing obligation from a command). Actual juristic rulings, such as 'the obligatory acts of ablution are six', are not themselves informational premises but conclusions of reasoning. Thus, logic provides the framework for all sound inference, exemplified by fiqh reasoning.

Key Terms
التصور
التصديق
التعاريف
الأقيسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Shirshimi's commentary, what is an example of a conceptual (tasawwur) element in a science?
A) The ruling that prayer is obligatory.
B) The definition of the term 'prayer'.
C) The syllogism proving the obligation of prayer.
D) The act of praying itself.

Key Takeaway
Conceptual knowledge in sciences is the grasp of term definitions; assensual knowledge is the acceptance of syllogistic proofs; actual rulings are the conclusions of such proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the following statement from fiqh: 'Riba is forbidden because it is a harmful increase.' Identify the tasawwur components (the terms defined) and the tasdiq component (the inference linking harm to prohibition). Then, using the lesson's distinction, explain why the actual ruling 'riba is forbidden' is a conclusion, not a premise.

What Is Mantiq?

5 min
Why Is Logic Called al-Mantiq? – The Three Meanings
Author lists the names of mantiq (al-miziq, al-mizan, miyar al-ulum) and explains why it is called 'mantiq'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three original meanings of the word 'mantiq' and the reason logic is named after them.

Core Idea
Logic is named 'al-mantiq' because it perfects perception, reason, and speech – the three core capacities of the human mind.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary on Bannani explains the names of logic and why it is called al-mantiq. The author shows that the word 'mantiq' originally referred to perception, the rational faculty, and speech – and the discipline of logic perfects all three. Understanding this etymology helps us appreciate the scope of logic as the tool of all sciences.

Guided Path
1
List the names of logic
The matn gives three names: al-mantiq, al-mizan (the scale), and miyar al-ulum (the standard of sciences). Note these are synonyms used by different authors.
Mizan and miyar emphasize logic's role as a measure for correct reasoning.
2
Identify the three original meanings of 'mantiq'
The passage explains that mantiq originally means: (1) idrak (perception), (2) al-quwwa al-aqila (the rational faculty), and (3) nutq (speech/utterance).
3
Connect each meaning to logic's function
The commentary says: by this discipline, perception increases and hits the mark; the rational faculty is strengthened and perfected; and the ability for speech is achieved. So logic improves all three.
The fronting in 'by it increases' (bihi yakthuru) is for emphasis—logic is the primary contributor but not the only one.
4
Examine the commentary on 'natiq' in the definition of man
The commentary clarifies that 'natiq' in 'insan natiq' means 'perceiving universal perceptions', not just speaking. This shows that the first meaning (perception) is fundamental.
Universal perception distinguishes humans from animals.
5
Analyze the linguistic forms of 'mantiq'
The passage notes that in the first and third meanings, 'mantiq' is a verbal noun (masdar mimi); in the second meaning, it is a noun of place. This shows the word's flexibility.
This linguistic detail is important for understanding its usage in other contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاسْمُهُ: «المَنْطِقُ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ، وَيُسَمَّى أَيْضاً بـ: المِيزَانِ»، وَبِـ: «مِعْيَارِ العُلُومِ». وَإِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ بـ : المَنْطِقِ»؛ لِأَنَّ المَنْطِقَ فِي الأَصْلِ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى : الإِدْرَاكِ) ، وَعَلَى : القُوَّةِ العَاقِلَةِ، وَعَلَى : النُّطْقِ الَّذِي هُوَ التَّلَفُظُ، وَهَذَا الفَنُّ بِهِ يَكْثُرُ الإِدْرَاكُ وَيُصِيبُ (٤) ، وَبِهِ تَتَقَوَى القُوَّةُ العَاقِلَةُ وَتَكْمُلُ، وَبِهِ تَكُونُ القُدْرَةُ عَلَى النُّطْقِ ، فَلَمَّا كَانَ لَهُ ارْتِبَاطُ بِكُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ المَعَانِي الثَّلَاثَةِ سُمِّيَ بِذَلِكَ. قوله : (وَبِ: مِعْيَارِ العُلُومِ») أي : ميزان الإدراكات الذي يعرف به صحيحها من فاسدها. قوله : (يُطْلَقُ عَلَى : الإِدْرَاكِ) ومنه نَاطِقٌ» في تعريف الإِنْسَان»؛ أي: مُدْرِك إدراكاً كليا؛ أي: كثيراً . وخرج بـ «كُلّيّا»: إدراك غير الإنسان مِنَ الحَيَوَانات، فلا يسمى: «منطقاً» و: «نطقاً»، وهو على هذا مصدر ميمي، كما هو على الإطلاق الثَّالث كذلك، بخلافه على الثاني، فإنَّه اسم مكان. قوله : (وَعَلَى : القُوَّةِ العَاقِلَةِ أي التي هي محل صدور تلك الإدراكات. قوله : (بِهِ يَكْثُرُ) قيل : تقديم المعمول في المواضع الثَّلاثة؛ للاهتمام، لا للحصر؛ إذ لغير المنطق دخل أيضاً، وإن كان هو أدخل . قوله : (تَكُونُ القُدْرَةُ) أي: التَّامَّة.
And its name: 'al-mantiq' as the author mentioned, and it is also called 'al-mizan' (the scale), and 'miyar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). It is called 'al-mantiq' only because mantiq originally applies to: perception (idrak), and to the rational faculty (al-quwwa al-aqila), and to speech (nutq) which is utterance. And this discipline by it perception increases and hits the mark, and by it the rational faculty is strengthened and perfected, and by it the ability for speech occurs. So when it has a connection with each of these three meanings, it was named by that. His saying: (and by miyar al-ulum) means: the scale of perceptions by which the sound is known from the unsound. His saying: (applies to perception) and from it is 'natiq' in the definition of man; i.e., perceiving a universal perception; i.e., much. And by 'universal' is excluded the perception of animals other than humans, so it is not called 'mantiq' and 'nutq'. And it is in this usage a verbal noun (masdar mimi), as it is in the third usage, unlike the second usage, for it is a noun of place. His saying: (and on the rational faculty) i.e., which is the locus of the issuance of those perceptions. His saying: (by it increases) it is said: the delayed object is fronted in the three instances for importance, not for restriction; since other than logic also has a role, although logic is more central. His saying: (the ability occurs) i.e., perfect ability.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage explains the names of the discipline of logic and the reason for its primary name. The matn states that logic is called 'al-mantiq', also 'al-mizan' (the scale), and 'miyar al-ulum' (the standard of sciences). The reason it is called 'al-mantiq' is because the Arabic word 'mantiq' originally has three meanings: (1) perception (idrak), (2) the rational faculty (al-quwwa al-aqila), and (3) speech/utterance (nutq). Logic relates to all three: it increases and sharpens perception, it strengthens the rational faculty, and it enables proper speech. Thus, the name is fitting. The commentary expands on each meaning. First, 'perception' is illustrated by the term 'natiq' in the definition of man (insan natiq), meaning a being that perceives universal concepts—a kind of perception specific to humans, excluding animals. This usage of 'mantiq' is a verbal noun (masdar mimi), like the third meaning. The second meaning—'rational faculty'—is a noun of place (ism makan) denoting the locus of perception. The commentary notes that in the statement 'by it perception increases', the fronting (taqdim) of the object ('by it') is for emphasis, not for restriction, because other disciplines also contribute, but logic plays the most significant role. Finally, 'the ability for speech' refers to perfect ability (al-tamma) to articulate ideas correctly, which logic fosters.

Key Terms
المَنْطِق
المِيزَان
مِعْيَار العُلُوم
النُّطْق

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One who perceives universal perceptions
C) One who has the power of speech
D) One who argues correctly

Key Takeaway
Logic is called al-mantiq because it perfects the three functions of the human mind: perception, reason, and speech.

What Is Mantiq?

Mantiq's Relation to the Heart like Nahw to the Tongue
Author defines the relationship of mantiq to the heart (jinan) analogously to nahw and the tongue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy between mantiq and nahw, and define the term 'jinan' as used in logic.

Core Idea
Logic regulates thought as grammar regulates speech.

The opening couplet of the matn establishes a powerful analogy: logic is to the heart (the seat of understanding) as grammar is to the tongue. But what exactly is the 'heart' in this context? The commentary unpacks this term, revealing a sophisticated understanding of the human intellectual and spiritual faculties. This lesson will help you grasp the analogy and the precise meaning of jinan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core analogy
Recognize the parallel: mantiq is to jinan (heart) as nahw (grammar) is to lisan (tongue). This means logic ensures correct thinking just as grammar ensures correct speech.
The analogy is the central thesis of the passage.
2
Analyze the grammatical construction
The phrase 'for the heart' (lil-jinan) is a circumstantial clause (hal) attached to an omitted predicate 'ascribed' (mansuban). This construction emphasizes the relationship.
According to Sibawayh's grammar, this is a permissible construction.
3
Examine the two interpretations of jinan
The commentator gives two meanings: (1) the intellect (dhan) metaphorically, i.e., the faculty of understanding; (2) the heart literally, but as the divine subtle substance (al-latifa al-rabbaniyya), not the physical organ.
The physical heart is a distinct meaning of qalb, not jinan in this context.
4
Understand the metaphorical transfer
Calling the intellect 'jinan' is a metaphor: the term for the spiritual substance (the real heart) is used for the attached faculty (the intellect). This is a common linguistic transfer.
This shows the integration of metaphysical anthropology into logic.
5
Summarize the three terms
Jinan: either the intellect metaphorically or the subtle substance literally. Dhan: the intellect, attached to jinan. Qalb: can refer to the subtle substance (literally) or the physical organ (literally).
Clarity on these terms is essential for reading classical logic texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَعْدُ: فَالمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِلِلِّسَانِ. قوله : (لِلْجَنَانِ) مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِمَحْذُوفٍ حَالٌ مِنَ المُبْتَدَأَ عَلَى طَرِيقَةِ مَنْ يُجِيزُهُ كَسِيْبَوَيْهِ؛ تَقْدِيرُهُ : مَنْسُوباً . وَالمُرَادُ بِـ الجَنَانِ» : الذَّهْنُ المُتَعَلِّقُ بِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ العَقْلُ مَجَازاً . أَوِ القَلْبُ حَقِيقَةٌ، لَكِنْ بِمَعْنَى : اللَّطِيفَةِ الرَّبَّانِيَّةِ. قوله : (مجازاً) راجع لقوله : «الذَّهْن»؛ أي: من باب تسمية المتعلّق - بالكسر ـ وهو الذهن باسم المتعلق - بالفتح - وهو الجَنَان؛ بمعنى : اللطيفة التي تسمى: «روحاً» و «نفساً» و: «قلباً» حقيقة، وكما يطلق القلب على تلك اللطيفة يُطلقُ على متعلَّقها وهو اللحمةُ الصَّنوبريَّة الشَّكل حقيقةً أيضاً . فتَلخّص : أنَّ الجَنّان يُطلق على اللطيفة بأسمائها حقيقةً، وعلى الذهن المتعلّق بها مجازاً، وأنَّ القلب يُطلق على اللطيفة المذكورة، وعلى متعلقها حقيقةً أيضاً، وأنَّ الذهن بمعنى: العقل . قوله : (أَوِ القَلْبُ) عطف على الذهن، لا على العقل. قوله : (الرَّبَّانِيَّةِ)
And after: the logic for the heart its relationship is like grammar for the tongue. His saying: (for the heart) is attached to an omitted word, a circumstantial clause from the subject according to the way of those who permit it like Sibawayh; its estimated form is: 'ascribed'. And what is meant by 'the heart' is: the intellect (dhan) attached to it, which is the mind metaphorically. Or the heart literally, but in the meaning of the divine subtle substance. His saying: (metaphorically) refers back to his saying: 'the intellect'; i.e., it is from the category of naming the object of attachment (the intellect) by the name of the thing to which it is attached (the heart); meaning: the subtle substance called 'spirit', 'soul', and 'heart' literally, and just as the heart is applied to that subtle substance, it is also applied to its object of attachment, which is the pinecone-shaped piece of flesh, literally as well. So the summary is: that 'jinan' is applied to the subtle substance with its names literally, and to the intellect attached to it metaphorically; and that 'heart' (qalb) is applied to the mentioned subtle substance and to its object of attachment also literally; and that 'intellect' (dhan) is in the meaning of mind ('aql). His saying: (or the heart) is an apposition to 'intellect', not to 'mind'. His saying: (divine).
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage defines the relationship of mantiq to the human faculty of understanding. The matn line states that mantiq stands to the heart (jinan) as nahw (grammar) stands to the tongue—meaning just as grammar regulates speech, logic regulates thought. The commentary then unpacks the term 'jinan'. First, it explains the grammatical construction: 'for the heart' is a circumstantial clause modifying an omitted predicate, 'ascribed'. Then it gives two possible meanings of jinan: (1) the intellect (dhan) attached to the heart, which is the mind ('aql) metaphorically; (2) the heart (qalb) literally, but in the sense of the divine subtle substance (al-latifa al-rabbaniyya), which is the spiritual essence. The commentator further clarifies that calling the intellect 'jinan' is a metaphorical transfer: the term for the subtle substance (the real heart) is used for its attached faculty (the intellect). Similarly, 'heart' (qalb) can refer both to the subtle substance and to the physical organ (the pinecone-shaped flesh) literally. Thus, the passage establishes that logic is the tool that ensures correct thinking, just as grammar ensures correct speech, and the heart/mind is the seat of that thinking.

Key Terms
الجَنَان
الذَّهْن
اللَّطِيفَة الرَّبَّانِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the literal meaning of 'jinan' when taken as 'heart'?
A) The physical pinecone-shaped organ
B) The intellect (dhan)
C) The divine subtle substance (al-latifa al-rabbaniyya)
D) The tongue (lisan)

Key Takeaway
Logic is the grammar of the mind, and the 'heart' (jinan) in this context is either the intellectual faculty metaphorically or the spiritual subtle substance literally.

The Source, Ruling, and Subject Matter of Logic
Author states the source, ruling, and subject matter of logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the source, ruling, and subject matter of logic as defined in the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Logic's authority comes from the intellect; it studies the forms of definitions and arguments.

This passage gives the foundational parameters of the science of logic (mantiq) as understood in the Islamic scholarly tradition. It clarifies where logic gets its principles, whether it is permissible to study, and what exactly it investigates. Understanding these three points is essential before engaging with any logical content, because they determine the epistemological status and boundaries of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source (istimdad)
Find where the text says logic derives its principles. The phrase is 'min al-'aql' (from the intellect). This distinguishes logic from revelation-based sciences like fiqh.
2
Identify the ruling (hukm)
Look for the legal assessment of studying logic. The text says 'al-jawaz' (permissibility). This indicates it is not obligatory nor forbidden.
3
Identify the subject matters (masa'il)
What does logic study? The text says 'theoretical propositions that examine the form of definitions and syllogisms'. So logic analyzes the structure of definitions and arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنِسْبَتُهُ لِلعُلُومِ مُبَايَنَتُهُ لَهَا (١) . وَاسْتِمْدَادُهُ : مِنَ العَقْلِ. وَحُكْمُهُ : الجَوَازُ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي. وَمَسَائِلُهُ : القَضَايَا النَّظَرِيَّةُ البَاحِثَةُ عَنْ هَيئَةِ المُعَرِّفَاتِ وَالأَقْيسَةِ وَمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِمَا . اهـ مُلَخَّصاً مِنْ شَرْحِ الشَّيْخ المَلوِيِّ الكَبِيرِ وَالصَّغِيرِ مَعَ زِيَادَةٍ (٢).
And its relationship to the sciences is its difference from them. And its source: from the intellect. And its ruling: permissibility as will come. And its subject matters: the theoretical propositions that examine the form of definitions and syllogisms and what relates to them. End. Summarized from the commentary of Shaykh al-Malwi, the major and minor, with additions.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage encapsulates the foundational aspects of the science of logic. First, it states that logic's relationship to other sciences is one of difference (mubayana)—it is distinct from them in its subject and purpose. Second, its source (istimdad) is the intellect (al-'aql), meaning its principles are derived from rational reflection rather than revelation or empirical data. Third, its ruling (hukm) is permissibility (jawaz), indicating that studying logic is permissible in Islam (as will be explained later in the text). Fourth, its subject matters (masa'il) are the theoretical propositions that investigate the forms (hay'a) of definitions (mu'arrafat) and syllogisms (aqisa), along with related topics. The parentheses indicate that the text is summarized from al-Malwi's commentaries, with additional glosses. The marginalia by al-Shirshimi elaborates that 'theoretical propositions' refers to those indicating universal relations that enter into the definition of logic itself. The passage thus gives a concise outline: logic is a distinct rational science, permissible to study, and its content is the structure of definitions and arguments.

Key Terms
الاِسْتِمْدَاد
الحُكْم
المَسَائِل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the source (istimdad) of logic?
A) The Qur'an and Sunnah
B) The intellect ('aql)
C) Consensus of scholars (ijma')
D) The sayings of the early Muslims

Key Takeaway
Logic is a rational science permissible to study, and its subject is the form of definitions and arguments.

?

The Two Meanings of al-Janān in Logic
Defining 'janān' and its referents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the metaphorical and literal meanings of 'al-janān' as used in the commentary and explain why the physical heart is excluded.

Core Idea
Logic protects the mind, not the physical heart.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a term that might easily be misunderstood: 'janān'. While commonly translated as 'heart', in logical works it refers to the intellect or the spiritual subtle substance, not the pinecone-shaped organ. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines what logic actually protects.

Guided Path
1
Locate 'al-janān' in the source
Find the term in the Arabic passage. Note the grammatical analysis provided.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The commentator gives two possibilities: metaphorically it is the intellect (al-dhihn), literally it is the divine subtle substance (al-latīfa al-rabbāniyya).
3
Distinguish the physical from the spiritual
The commentator explicitly rejects the physical heart (the pinecone-shaped organ) as the intended meaning. He describes the physical heart to contrast it with the spiritual meaning.
4
Understand why this distinction matters in logic
Logic deals with mental concepts and reasoning, not bodily organs. Therefore, 'janān' in logic must refer to the intellectual or spiritual faculty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (لِلْجَنَانِ) مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِمَحْذُوفٍ حَالٌ مِنَ المُبْتَدَأَ عَلَى طَرِيقَةِ مَنْ يُجِيزُهُ كَسِيْبَوَيْهِ؛ تَقْدِيرُهُ : مَنْسُوباً ، كَمَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ الشَّيْخُ المَلَّوِيُّ ، أَوْ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِقَوْلِهِ بَعْدُ : «نِسْبَتُهُ» كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ .
وَالمُرَادُ بِـ الجَنَانِ» : الذَّهْنُ المُتَعَلِّقُ بِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ العَقْلُ مَجَازاً . أَوِ القَلْبُ حَقِيقَةٌ، لَكِنْ بِمَعْنَى : اللَّطِيفَةِ الرَّبَّانِيَّةِ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى : رُوحاً» و «نَفْساً»، لَا بِمَعْنَى : اللُّحْمَةِ الصَّنَوبَرِيَّةِ الشَّكْلِ ; أَي: الَّتِي شَكْلُهَا كَشَكُل الصَّنَوبَرِ، وَهُوَ شَجَرٌ يَنْبُتُ فِي البَرِيَّةِ، دَقِيقُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ، غَلِيظُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَارَةِ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، فَهَذِهِ اللُّحْمَةِ عَلَى هَذَا الشَّكْلِ، فَهِيَ دَقِيقَةُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ غَلِيظَةُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَارَةٍ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، كَمَا يُشَاهَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي قَلْبِ الدَّجَاجَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا.
قَوْلُهُ : (نِسْبَتُهُ) أَي : المَنْطِقِ .
وَقَوْلُهُ : (كَالنَّحْوِ) أَيْ : كَنِسْبَةِ النَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ.
وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ التَّشْبِيهَ إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي أَصْلِ العِصْمَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَالمَنْطِقُ يَعْصِمُ الجَنَانَ عَنِ الخَطَأ في الفِكْرِ، وَالنَّحْو يَعْصِمُ اللَّسَانَ عَنِ الخَطأ في الكَلَامِ.
His statement: 'to the heart' is attached to an omitted word, being a circumstantial accusative from the subject, according to the way of those who permit it like Sibawayh; its implicit meaning: 'ascribed'. As pointed out by al-Mallawi, or it is attached to his statement later: 'its relation' as some said. And what is meant by 'the heart': the intellect attached to it, which is the mind, metaphorically; or the heart, literally, but in the sense of the divine subtle substance which is called 'spirit' and 'soul', not in the sense of the pinecone-shaped flesh; i.e., that whose shape is like the shape of the pinecone, which is a tree that grows in the wilderness, narrow at one end, thick at the other with a kind of roundness like a sugar funnel; so this flesh is of this shape, being narrow at one end, thick at the other with a kind of roundness like a sugar funnel, as is observed in the heart of a chicken and others. His statement: 'its relation' means: of logic. And his statement: 'like grammar' means: like the relation of grammar to the tongue. And it is not hidden that the comparison is only in the principle of protection, for logic protects the heart from error in thinking, and grammar protects the tongue from error in speech.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on a line from the matn of al-Sullam. The commentator, likely al-Bajuri or al-Bannani, explains the phrase 'to the heart' (للجنان). He presents two grammatical analyses: either it is a circumstantial accusative modifying the implied subject (as Sibawayh would permit), meaning 'ascribed', or it attaches to the later phrase 'its relation'. The commentator then defines 'janan' (heart/intellect). He states that it can refer metaphorically to the intellect attached to the heart, or literally to the 'subtle divine substance' (al-latifa al-rabbaniyya) called spirit and soul, not the physical pinecone-shaped organ. He elaborates that this subtle substance is called 'heart' in a true sense, but the physical heart is also called 'heart' literally. The passage then clarifies the analogy: the comparison between logic and grammar is only in their function of protection ('isma). Logic protects the mind (janan) from error in thinking, while grammar protects the tongue from error in speech. The commentary emphasizes the precise meanings to avoid confusion between the physical organ and the spiritual faculty.

Key Terms
الجَنَان
القَلْب
الذَّهْن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The divine subtle substance (al-latīfa al-rabbāniyya)

Key Takeaway
In logic, 'al-janān' refers either metaphorically to the intellect or literally to the spiritual substance, never to the physical heart.

The Protective Analogy Between Logic and Grammar
Analogy between logic and grammar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy between logic and grammar in terms of their protective function and apply it to evaluate other disciplines.

Core Idea
Logic protects the mind from error just as grammar protects the tongue.

The commentary draws a clear analogy: logic safeguards the mind (janān) from error in thinking, while grammar safeguards the tongue from error in speech. This comparison highlights the instrumental role of logic as a tool for correct reasoning, akin to grammar for correct expression. Understanding this analogy helps situate logic within the broader Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items being compared
Find 'logic' (al-mantiq) and 'grammar' (al-nahw) in the passage.
2
Identify the basis of comparison
The passage states the comparison is in 'the principle of protection' (al-'isma).
3
Note what each protects
Logic protects the 'janān' (heart/mind) from error in thinking; grammar protects the 'lisān' (tongue) from error in speech.
4
Understand the domains
The domain of logic is inner mental thought (al-fikr); the domain of grammar is outer verbal expression (al-kalām).
5
Reflect on the implication
This analogy shows that logic is a normative discipline for correct reasoning, just as grammar is for correct speech.

وَالمُرَادُ بِـ الجَنَانِ» : الذَّهْنُ المُتَعَلِّقُ بِهِ الَّذِي هُوَ العَقْلُ مَجَازاً . أَوِ القَلْبُ حَقِيقَةٌ، لَكِنْ بِمَعْنَى : اللَّطِيفَةِ الرَّبَّانِيَّةِ الَّتِي تُسَمَّى : رُوحاً» و «نَفْساً»، لَا بِمَعْنَى : اللُّحْمَةِ الصَّنَوبَرِيَّةِ الشَّكْلِ ; أَي: الَّتِي شَكْلُهَا كَشَكُل الصَّنَوبَرِ، وَهُوَ شَجَرٌ يَنْبُتُ فِي البَرِيَّةِ، دَقِيقُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ، غَلِيظُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَارَةِ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، فَهَذِهِ اللُّحْمَةِ عَلَى هَذَا الشَّكْلِ، فَهِيَ دَقِيقَةُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ غَلِيظَةُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَارَةٍ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، كَمَا يُشَاهَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي قَلْبِ الدَّجَاجَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا.

Logic and Grammar: Protecting Mind and Tongue
Introduces the metaphor comparing logic to grammar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of logic using the grammar analogy and identify the key terms mantiq, janaan, nahw, and isma.

Core Idea
Logic protects the mind from error just as grammar protects the tongue.

This lesson unpacks the classic opening metaphor of many logic texts: logic's relation to the heart is like grammar's relation to the tongue. The author grounds this comparison in the concept of 'isma (protection). Understanding this analogy helps you see the practical purpose of logic within the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sciences being compared
The passage compares mantiq (logic) and nahw (Arabic grammar). Both are sciences that provide rules to avoid error.
2
Identify the two organs they protect
Logic protects the janaan (spiritual heart, seat of intellect), grammar protects the lisaan (tongue, organ of speech).
The heart here is not the physical heart but the subtle entity called ruh or nafs.
3
Extract the shared function: ismah
Both sciences provide ismah (protection): logic prevents error in thought (fikr), grammar prevents error in speech (kalaam).
4
Note the grammatical analysis of the line
The author offers two possible readings of the Arabic syntax. The second reading, with 'nisbatu' directly connected, is preferred as less forced.
This step is optional; focus on the conceptual analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَعْدُ: فَالْمَنْطِقُ لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ. نِسْبَتُهُ كَالنَّحْوِ لِلِّسَانِ
الباجوري
الَّتِي تُسَمَّى : رُوحاً و «نَفْساً»، لَا بِمَعْنَى : اللُّحْمَةِ الصَّنَوبَرِيَّةِ الشَّكْلِ ؛ أَي: الَّتِي شَكْلُهَا كَشَكُل الصَّنَوبَرِ، وَهُوَ شَجَرٌ يَنْبُتُ فِي البَرِيَّةِ، دَقِيقُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ، غَلِيظُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَارَةِ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، فَهَذِهِ اللُّحْمَةِ عَلَى هَذَا الشَّكْلِ، فَهِيَ دَقِيقَةُ أَحَدِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ غَلِيظَةُ الآخَرِ مَعَ نَوْعِ اسْتِدَرَاةٍ كَقُمْعِ السُّكَرِ، كَمَا يُشَاهَدُ ذَلِكَ فِي قَلْبِ الدَّجَاجَةِ وَغَيْرِهَا
قَوْلُهُ : (نِسْبَتُهُ) أَي : المَنْطِقِ .
وَقَوْلُهُ : (كَالنَّحْوِ) أَيْ : كَنِسْبَةِ النَّحْوِ ؛ كَمَا قَدَّرَهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ، لِيَتَنَاسَبَ المُشَبَّهُ وَالمُشَبَّهُ وَقَوْلُهُ : (لِلِّسَانِ) مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِمَحْذُوفٍ حَالٌ مِنَ النَّحْوِ؛ تَقْدِيرُهُ : مَنْسُوباً ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى جَعْلٍ قَوْلِهِ : لِلْجَنَانِ مُتَعَلِّقاً بِمَحْذُوفٍ، أَوْ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِلَفْظ «نِسْبَة) المُقَدَّرِ ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى جَعْلٍ ذَلِكَ مُتَعَلِّقاً بِقَوْلِهِ : «نسبته»
وَتَقْدِيرُ المَتْنِ عَلَى الأَوَّلِ : فَالمَنْطِقُ حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مَنْسُوباً لِلْجَنَانِ نِسْبَتُهُ كَنِسْبَةِ النَّحْوِ حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مَنْسُوباً لِلَّسَانِ.
وَعَلَى الثَّانِي: فَالمَنْطِقُ نِسْبَتُهُ لِلْجَنَانِ كَنِسْبَةِ النَّحْوِ لِلْسَانِ، وَهَذَا أَقَلُّ تَكلُّفاً مِنَ الأَوَّلِ. وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ التَّشْبِيهَ إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي أَصْلِ العِصْمَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَالمَنْطِقُ يَعْصِمُ الجَنَانَ عَنِ الخَطَأ في الفِكْرِ، وَالنَّحْو يَعْصِمُ اللَّسَانَ عَنِ الخَطأ في الكَلَامِ، كَمَا أَشَارَ لِذَلِكَ بِالتَّفْرِيع.
الأنبابي
أي : المنسوبة للرَّبِّ، بزيادة الألف والنون على غير قياس؛ للمبالغة. ونسبها إليه ؛ لأنَّه لا يعلمها إلا هو سبحانه وتعالى، أو لأنَّ الجوهر المجرَّد ليس متحيزاً، ولا قائماً بمتحيِّز، كما أنَّ الرَّبَّ سبحانه وتعالى كذلك.
قوله : (الَّتِي تُسَمَّى : رُوحاً... إلخ) هذا مبني على اتحاد الرُّوح والنَّفس، وهو الصحيح. وقيل: الرُّوحُ ما به الحياة، والنَّفس ما به تدبير البدن .
And after: Logic's relation to the heart is like grammar's relation to the tongue. [Bajuri continues explaining that the heart referred to is the spiritual entity called ruh and nafs, not the pinecone-shaped flesh; that heart is shaped like a pinecone, a tree that grows in the desert, thin at one end, thick at the other with a kind of roundness like a sugar cone, and this flesh is on this shape, as seen in the heart of a chicken and others. He says: 'His statement: (nusbatuhu) means: of logic.' And his statement: (ka al-nahwi) means: like the relation of grammar, as Shaykh al-Mallawi estimated, so that the compared and the comparator are proportional. His statement: (lil-lisani) is connected to an implied present participle from 'al-nahwi', its implied meaning: 'being relative', based on taking his statement 'lil-janani' as connected to an implied present participle, or it is connected to the implied word 'nisba', based on taking that as connected to his statement 'nisbatahu'. The estimation of the matn on the first is: logic, while being relative to the heart, its relation is like the relation of grammar while being relative to the tongue. And on the second: logic's relation to the heart is like grammar's relation to the tongue, and this is less forced than the first. It is not hidden that the comparison is only in the basis of protection (ismah); otherwise logic protects the heart from error in thought, and grammar protects the tongue from error in speech, as he indicated by the consequence (tafrie). [Anbabi says: meaning: attributed to the Lord, with an extra alif and nun irregularly for exaggeration. And He attributed them to Himself because no one knows them except Him, or because the simple substance (jawhar mujarrad) is not spatial nor subsisting in a spatial entity, just as the Lord is like that. His statement: 'which is called ruh... etc.' is based on the unity of ruh and nafs, which is correct. And it is said: ruh is that by which life exists, and nafs is that by which the body is managed.]
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening line of the matn, which states that logic's relation to the heart (janaan) is like grammar's relation to the tongue. The author first clarifies that the 'heart' here refers to the spiritual subtlety (al-latifa al-rabbaniyya) called ruh and nafs, not the physical heart shaped like a pinecone. He then provides a detailed grammatical analysis of the line, offering two possible readings: one treating 'lil-janani' as a circumstantial qualifier (hal) of 'mantiq', and the other as directly connected to an implied 'nisba'. The second reading is preferred as less forced. The core of the comparison is the concept of 'ismah' (protection): logic protects the intellect from error in thinking, just as grammar protects the tongue from error in speech. A marginal note by al-Anbabi further explains that the heart (ruh/nafs) is attributed to Allah to indicate its nobility and its non-physical nature, akin to the simple substance that is not spatial. The discussion on the unity of ruh and nafs is also noted, with the alternative view distinguishing them by function.

Key Terms
مَنْطِق
جَنَان
نَحْو
عِصْمَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the comparison of logic to grammar primarily indicate?
A) That logic is a branch of grammar.
B) That both logic and grammar provide protection against error.
C) That logic is superior to grammar.
D) That the heart and tongue are equal in importance.

Key Takeaway
Logic, like grammar for speech, protects the intellect from error and is indispensable for sound reasoning in the Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own words, explain how logic and grammar are similar in their protective function. Provide an example from Islamic theology where logic helps avoid an error in reasoning.
?
Identify the key terms (mantiq, janaan, nahw, isma) in the opening line of the matn and explain their significance based on the commentary.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate

Linguistic vs. Legal 'Isma: Why the Meaning Matters
Bajuri defines 'isma and distinguishes linguistic vs legal meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the linguistic meaning of 'isma (absolute preservation) from its legal meaning (infallibility) and explain the implications for dua and for understanding logic's role.

Core Idea
'Isma in logic is linguistic preservation, not prophetic infallibility.

In his commentary on al-Sullam, Bajuri clarifies that the term 'isma in the phrase 'it preserves the intellect' is used in its linguistic sense of absolute preservation, not the legal sense of infallibility specific to prophets. This distinction is crucial because it determines whether it is permissible to ask Allah for 'isma in prayer. Let's unpack this distinction and see why it matters for understanding logic's role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings of 'isma
Find where Bajuri states that 'isma here is linguistic, not legal. Note the definitions: linguistic = 'absolute preservation', legal = 'preservation from something with impossibility of its occurrence'.
Look for the phrase 'بِمَعْنَاهَا اللُّغَوِيٌّ' and 'بِمَعْنَاهَا الشَّرْعِيِّ'.
2
Determine the scope of each meaning
The legal meaning is specific to prophets and angels; saints are preserved (mahfuz) but not infallible (ma'sum). The linguistic meaning is general.
3
Apply the distinction to the permissibility of asking for 'isma
Bajuri says that asking for 'isma in the legal sense (like 'O Allah, grant me infallibility') is not permissible for non-prophets, but asking in the linguistic sense (preservation) is fine. Why? Because legal 'isma implies impossibility of sin, which is exclusive to prophets.
Reflect on the difference between 'اعصمني' and 'ارزقني العصمة'.
4
Connect to logic
Logic preserves the intellect in the linguistic sense: it protects from error when observed, but not absolutely or with impossibility of error.
This shows that logic is a tool, not a guarantee of infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (فَيَعْصِمُ ... إلخ) مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّشْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ وَالمُرَادُ : أَنَّهُ يَعْصِمُ عِنْدَ مُرَاعَاتِهِ وَمُلَا حَظَتِهِ ، فَهُوَ العَاصِمُ لَكِنْ بِشَرْطِ المُرَاعَاةِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ، وَهُوَ أَوْجَهُ (٢) مِمَّا اشْتُهِرَ مِنْ جَعْلِ العَاصِمِ نَفْسَ المُرَاعَاةِ . وَالعِصْمَةُ هُنَا بِمَعْنَاهَا اللُّغَوِيٌّ وَهُوَ: «مُطْلَقُ الحِفْظِ»، لَا بِمَعْنَاهَا الشَّرْعِيِّ وَهُوَ : الحِفْظُ مِنَ الشَّيْء مَعَ اسْتِحَالَةِ وُقُوعِهِ مِنَ المَعْصُومِ ، وَهِيَ بِهَذَا المَعْنَى مُخْتَصَّةٌ بِالأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالمَلَائِكَةِ دُونَ الأَوْلِيَاءِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ مَحْفُوظُونَ لا مَعْصُومُونَ، وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ سُؤَالُ العِصْمَةِ ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «اللَّهُمَّ اعْصِمْنِي مِنَ المَعَاصِي ، أَوْ: «اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ العِصْمَةَ إِذَا أُرِيدَ المَعْنَى الشَّرْعِيُّ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أُرِيدَ المَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيُّ.
الأنبابي
قوله : (مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّشْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ) في تفريع عصمة الفكر على التشبيه المذكور خفاء؛ إذ لم يفهم منه ذلك، كما أنَّ في تفريع كشف المنطق للغطاء عن المسائل الصَّعبة خفاء أيضاً؛ إلا أن ينظر في الأول لمطلق العصمة، أو لقوله : للجنان»، وينظر في الثاني لكون النَّحو يكشف للسان صواب أمكنة البحث، فيكون وجه الشَّبه أمرين : مطلق العصمة، ومطلق الكشف لا أصل العصمة [ج/ ١١] ،فقط كما قاله المحشي أولاً، ولا يقال : أنَّ الكشف لازم للعصمة، أو يقال : أَنَّ قوله : وَعَنْ دَقِيقِ الفَهْم ... إلخ » كلام مستأنف، لا معطوف على التفريع.
قوله : (فَهُوَ العَاصِمُ) في إسناد العصمة» إلى المنطق»، أو إلى مراعاته مجاز عقليّ؛ إذ العاصم هو الله
تعالى، والمنطقُ عند مراعاته آلةٌ في العصمة، فالعصمة لا تنسب إليه مجازاً إِلَّا عند مراعاته . قوله : (وَهُوَ [ب/ ١٦] أَوْجَهُ) أي : لأنَّ الإسناد إلى السَّبب أَوْلى مِنَ الإسناد إلى الشَّرط.
(۱) الشرشيمي : قوله : (مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّنْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ) لا يظهر تفريعه على التّشبيه إلَّا بالنظر لمطلق العصمة، وأما تفريعه بالنَّظر الأفكار فلا يصح؛ لأنَّه لم يفهم مِنَ التَّشبيه ؛ إلا أن ينظر إلى قوله : للجنان» فيصح تفريع ذلك بتمامه. وأما قوله : وعن دقيق الفهم ... إلخ » لم يتفرع على ما قبله أصلاً؛ إلا أن يقال : إنَّ وجه الشبه فيما سبق يجعل عاما بأن يقال : إنَّه كالنَّحو في العصمة وفي إزالة الصُّعوبة ؛ لأنَّ النَّحو يزيل الصعوبة عن اللسان .
(۲) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَهُوَ أَوْجَهُ أي : لأنَّ العاصم حقيقةً هو الله تعالى، فالأنسبُ النِّسبة لآلته، لا لشرطه حيث أريد التَّجوز. [اهـ] عن بعضهم .
His statement: (For it preserves...) etc. is a branching from the mentioned simile. The meaning is that it preserves when one observes and takes it into account. So it is the preserver, but with the condition of observance, as some verifiers said. And it is more proper than what is known of making the preserver itself the observance. And 'isma here is in its linguistic sense, which is absolute preservation, not in its legal sense which is preservation from a thing coupled with the impossibility of its occurrence from the preserved one. And it in this sense is specific to prophets and angels, not to saints, for they are preserved, not infallible. For this reason, asking for 'isma is not permissible, such as saying 'O Allah, preserve me from sins' or 'O Allah, I ask You for 'isma' if the legal meaning is intended, contrary to when the linguistic meaning is intended. Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (branching from the mentioned simile) in branching the preservation of thought from the mentioned simile there is obscurity, for it is not understood from that, just as in branching logic's unveiling of the cover from difficult matters there is also obscurity; unless one considers in the first the absolute preservation, or his saying 'for the heart', and considers in the second that grammar unveils for the tongue the correctness of places of inquiry, so the point of similarity becomes two matters: absolute preservation and absolute unveiling, not the essence of preservation, as the commentator said first. And it is not said that unveiling is necessary for preservation, or that his statement 'and from subtle understanding...' is a new statement, not coordinated with the branching. His statement: (so it is the preserver) in attributing 'isma to logic or to its observance is a mental metaphor; for the preserver is Allah Almighty, and logic when observed is an instrument in preservation, so preservation is not attributed to it metaphorically except when observed. His statement: (and it [ب/ ١٦] is more proper) means because attribution to the cause is more appropriate than attribution to the condition. (1) Al-Sharshimi: His statement: (branching from the mentioned reminder) the branching from the simile does not appear except by consideration of absolute preservation. As for its branching by consideration of thoughts, it is not correct because it is not understood from the simile; unless one considers his saying 'for the heart', then that branching becomes complete. As for his saying 'and from subtle understanding...' it is not branched from what preceded at all; unless it is said that the point of similarity in what preceded is made general by saying it is like grammar in preservation and in removing difficulty, because grammar removes difficulty from the tongue. (2) Al-Sharshimi: His statement: (and it is more proper) means because the preserver in reality is Allah Almighty, so the most appropriate is to attribute to its instrument, not to its condition, when metaphor is intended. [End] from some of them.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn line 'فَيَعْصِمُ الأَفْكَارَ...' from al-Sullam. The commentators clarify that logic preserves the intellect only when one observes its rules; it is not inherently a preserver but becomes so through application. They argue it is more accurate to say that logic is the cause of preservation rather than that observance itself is the preserver. Then they define 'isma: here it is used in its linguistic sense of absolute preservation, not the legal sense of infallibility specific to prophets and angels. This distinction matters because asking for 'isma in the legal sense from Allah would be improper for non-prophets, whereas the linguistic sense is permissible. The sub-commentators (al-Anbabiy and al-Sharshimi) debate the branching of this line from the previous simile, noting obscurity and offering interpretations. Al-Anbabiy explains that the point of similarity is twofold: absolute preservation and absolute unveiling, not the essence. He also notes that attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor, as Allah is the true preserver. Al-Sharshimi adds that attributing to the instrument is more proper than to the condition when metaphor is intended.

معصوم
محفوظ
مطلق الحفظ
استحالة الوقوع

C) It means that logic itself is the preserver without condition.

Key Takeaway
When logic is said to preserve the intellect, 'isma means absolute preservation in the linguistic sense, not the infallibility specific to prophets.

What Is Mantiq?
advanced
10 min
Who Preserves? Logic, Allah, and the Condition of Observance
Bajuri and commentators discuss the attribution of preservation to logic as a mental metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor and why it is more proper to say logic is the cause (instrument) rather than the condition.

Core Idea
Logic preserves only when observed; Allah is the true Preserver.

Bajuri and his commentators debate a subtle point: should we say that logic itself is the preserver, or that observance of logic is the preserver? They conclude that attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor, and that it is more appropriate to call logic the instrument (cause) rather than the condition. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows its relevance to understanding the proper role of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on 'the preserver'
Some say 'the preserver is logic itself when observed'; others say 'the preserver is the observance itself'. Find where Bajuri states his preference and why.
Look for the phrase 'فَهُوَ العَاصِمُ لَكِنْ بِشَرْطِ المُرَاعَاةِ' and the criticism of making the preserver the observance itself.
2
Analyze the mental metaphor (majaz 'aqli)
Al-Anbabiy explains that attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor because the true preserver is Allah. In Arabic rhetoric, attributing an action to its instrument is a common metaphor.
Compare to 'الطبيب شاف' (the doctor heals) – Allah is the true healer.
3
Compare cause vs condition
Bajuri says attributing to the cause (logic as instrument) is 'more proper' than attributing to the condition (observance). A cause directly contributes to the effect, while a condition is external. Al-Sharshimi adds that attribution to the instrument is more appropriate when metaphor is intended.
Think: the observance is a condition for logic to work, but logic itself (when observed) is the proximate cause of preservation.
4
Apply to the broader aim of logic
This analysis shows that logic does not work automatically; the student must actively observe its rules. The preservation is conditional, not automatic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (فَيَعْصِمُ ... إلخ) مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّشْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ وَالمُرَادُ : أَنَّهُ يَعْصِمُ عِنْدَ مُرَاعَاتِهِ وَمُلَا حَظَتِهِ ، فَهُوَ العَاصِمُ لَكِنْ بِشَرْطِ المُرَاعَاةِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ، وَهُوَ أَوْجَهُ (٢) مِمَّا اشْتُهِرَ مِنْ جَعْلِ العَاصِمِ نَفْسَ المُرَاعَاةِ . وَالعِصْمَةُ هُنَا بِمَعْنَاهَا اللُّغَوِيٌّ وَهُوَ: «مُطْلَقُ الحِفْظِ»، لَا بِمَعْنَاهَا الشَّرْعِيِّ وَهُوَ : الحِفْظُ مِنَ الشَّيْء مَعَ اسْتِحَالَةِ وُقُوعِهِ مِنَ المَعْصُومِ ، وَهِيَ بِهَذَا المَعْنَى مُخْتَصَّةٌ بِالأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالمَلَائِكَةِ دُونَ الأَوْلِيَاءِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ مَحْفُوظُونَ لا مَعْصُومُونَ، وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوزُ سُؤَالُ العِصْمَةِ ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «اللَّهُمَّ اعْصِمْنِي مِنَ المَعَاصِي ، أَوْ: «اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ العِصْمَةَ إِذَا أُرِيدَ المَعْنَى الشَّرْعِيُّ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أُرِيدَ المَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيُّ.
الأنبابي
قوله : (مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّشْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ) في تفريع عصمة الفكر على التشبيه المذكور خفاء؛ إذ لم يفهم منه ذلك، كما أنَّ في تفريع كشف المنطق للغطاء عن المسائل الصَّعبة خفاء أيضاً؛ إلا أن ينظر في الأول لمطلق العصمة، أو لقوله : للجنان»، وينظر في الثاني لكون النَّحو يكشف للسان صواب أمكنة البحث، فيكون وجه الشَّبه أمرين : مطلق العصمة، ومطلق الكشف لا أصل العصمة [ج/ ١١] ،فقط كما قاله المحشي أولاً، ولا يقال : أنَّ الكشف لازم للعصمة، أو يقال : أَنَّ قوله : وَعَنْ دَقِيقِ الفَهْم ... إلخ » كلام مستأنف، لا معطوف على التفريع.
قوله : (فَهُوَ العَاصِمُ) في إسناد العصمة» إلى المنطق»، أو إلى مراعاته مجاز عقليّ؛ إذ العاصم هو الله
تعالى، والمنطقُ عند مراعاته آلةٌ في العصمة، فالعصمة لا تنسب إليه مجازاً إِلَّا عند مراعاته . قوله : (وَهُوَ [ب/ ١٦] أَوْجَهُ) أي : لأنَّ الإسناد إلى السَّبب أَوْلى مِنَ الإسناد إلى الشَّرط.
(۱) الشرشيمي : قوله : (مُفَرَّعٌ عَلَى التَّنْبِيهِ المَذْكُورِ) لا يظهر تفريعه على التّشبيه إلَّا بالنظر لمطلق العصمة، وأما تفريعه بالنَّظر الأفكار فلا يصح؛ لأنَّه لم يفهم مِنَ التَّشبيه ؛ إلا أن ينظر إلى قوله : للجنان» فيصح تفريع ذلك بتمامه. وأما قوله : وعن دقيق الفهم ... إلخ » لم يتفرع على ما قبله أصلاً؛ إلا أن يقال : إنَّ وجه الشبه فيما سبق يجعل عاما بأن يقال : إنَّه كالنَّحو في العصمة وفي إزالة الصُّعوبة ؛ لأنَّ النَّحو يزيل الصعوبة عن اللسان .
(۲) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَهُوَ أَوْجَهُ أي : لأنَّ العاصم حقيقةً هو الله تعالى، فالأنسبُ النِّسبة لآلته، لا لشرطه حيث أريد التَّجوز. [اهـ] عن بعضهم .
His statement: (For it preserves...) etc. is a branching from the mentioned simile. The meaning is that it preserves when one observes and takes it into account. So it is the preserver, but with the condition of observance, as some verifiers said. And it is more proper than what is known of making the preserver itself the observance. And 'isma here is in its linguistic sense, which is absolute preservation, not in its legal sense which is preservation from a thing coupled with the impossibility of its occurrence from the preserved one. And it in this sense is specific to prophets and angels, not to saints, for they are preserved, not infallible. For this reason, asking for 'isma is not permissible, such as saying 'O Allah, preserve me from sins' or 'O Allah, I ask You for 'isma' if the legal meaning is intended, contrary to when the linguistic meaning is intended. Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (branching from the mentioned simile) in branching the preservation of thought from the mentioned simile there is obscurity, for it is not understood from that, just as in branching logic's unveiling of the cover from difficult matters there is also obscurity; unless one considers in the first the absolute preservation, or his saying 'for the heart', and considers in the second that grammar unveils for the tongue the correctness of places of inquiry, so the point of similarity becomes two matters: absolute preservation and absolute unveiling, not the essence of preservation, as the commentator said first. And it is not said that unveiling is necessary for preservation, or that his statement 'and from subtle understanding...' is a new statement, not coordinated with the branching. His statement: (so it is the preserver) in attributing 'isma to logic or to its observance is a mental metaphor; for the preserver is Allah Almighty, and logic when observed is an instrument in preservation, so preservation is not attributed to it metaphorically except when observed. His statement: (and it [ب/ ١٦] is more proper) means because attribution to the cause is more appropriate than attribution to the condition. (1) Al-Sharshimi: His statement: (branching from the mentioned reminder) the branching from the simile does not appear except by consideration of absolute preservation. As for its branching by consideration of thoughts, it is not correct because it is not understood from the simile; unless one considers his saying 'for the heart', then that branching becomes complete. As for his saying 'and from subtle understanding...' it is not branched from what preceded at all; unless it is said that the point of similarity in what preceded is made general by saying it is like grammar in preservation and in removing difficulty, because grammar removes difficulty from the tongue. (2) Al-Sharshimi: His statement: (and it is more proper) means because the preserver in reality is Allah Almighty, so the most appropriate is to attribute to its instrument, not to its condition, when metaphor is intended. [End] from some of them.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn line 'فَيَعْصِمُ الأَفْكَارَ...' from al-Sullam. The commentators clarify that logic preserves the intellect only when one observes its rules; it is not inherently a preserver but becomes so through application. They argue it is more accurate to say that logic is the cause of preservation rather than that observance itself is the preserver. Then they define 'isma: here it is used in its linguistic sense of absolute preservation, not the legal sense of infallibility specific to prophets and angels. This distinction matters because asking for 'isma in the legal sense from Allah would be improper for non-prophets, whereas the linguistic sense is permissible. The sub-commentators (al-Anbabiy and al-Sharshimi) debate the branching of this line from the previous simile, noting obscurity and offering interpretations. Al-Anbabiy explains that the point of similarity is twofold: absolute preservation and absolute unveiling, not the essence. He also notes that attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor, as Allah is the true preserver. Al-Sharshimi adds that attributing to the instrument is more proper than to the condition when metaphor is intended.

Key Terms
عاصم
مراعاة
مجاز عقلي
سبب
شرط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is attributing preservation to logic a mental metaphor?
A) Because logic is a physical thing that cannot preserve.
B) Because the true preserver is Allah, and logic is only an instrument.
C) Because observance is the real preserver.
D) Because preservation is not a real action.

Key Takeaway
Attributing preservation to logic is a mental metaphor; Allah is the true Preserver, and logic is merely an instrument that preserves only when its rules are observed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the following statement: 'Al-nahw (grammar) preserves the tongue from error.' Identify the mental metaphor and explain who the true preserver is.
?
Debate: Take the position that it is better to say 'observance of logic preserves' versus 'logic preserves when observed'. Which side does the commentary support and why?

Unveiling the Metaphor in Logic's Definition: Isti'ara bi-al-Kinaya
Explanation of the second hemistich and its isti'ara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of isti'ara bi-al-kinaya (implicit metaphor) in a logical definition and explain how it reinforces the meaning.

Core Idea
Logic unveils subtle truths, but the verse itself veils its meaning in metaphor.

In this lesson, we examine how the poet of the matn uses a sophisticated rhetorical device to describe what logic does. Al-Bajuri unpacks the second hemistich, showing that it is not a simple literal statement but an implicit metaphor. Understanding this rhetorical layer is essential for correctly interpreting the definition of mantiq.

Guided Path
1
Break down the grammar
Note that 'al-fahm' is interpreted as 'al-mafhum' (the understood thing), and 'daqiq al-fahm' is an adjective-noun construction. What is the literal rendering?
The idhafa is of the adjective to the described.
2
Identify the implicit simile (tashbih mudmar)
The author says the subtle understanding is likened to a covered thing. What is the shared feature? It needs unveiling.
The simile is implicit, not explicitly stated.
3
Locate the isti'ara bi-al-kinaya components
What is mentioned instead of the likened-to thing? The cover (ghita') and the unveiling (kashf) are concomitants of the covered thing. Why are they used?
The likened-to thing is omitted; only its concomitants are mentioned.
4
Distinguish takhyil and tarshih
The cover is takhyil (imaginative detail), the unveiling is tarshih (reinforcement). How do these enhance the metaphor?
Takhyil makes the metaphor vivid; tarshih extends it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : : (وَعَنْ دَقِيقِ الفَهْم ... إلخ) «الوَاوُ دَاخِلَةٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : يَكْشِفُ، وَالإِضَافَةُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : دَقِيقِ الفَهْمِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصَّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ وَالفَهُمُ بِمَعْنَى المَفْهُومِ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ حِينَئِذٍ : وَيَكْشِفُ الغِطَاءَ عَنِ المَفْهُومِ الدَّقِيقِ . وَفِي كَلَامِهِ اسْتِعَارَةٌ بِالكِنَايَةِ وَتَخْيِيلُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ شَبَّهَ دَقِيقَ الفَهْمِ بِشَيْءٍ مُغَطَّى تَشْبِيها مُضْمَراً فِي النَّفْسِ، وَحَذَفَ اسْمَ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ، وَأَثْبَتَ شَيْئاً مِنْ لَوَازِمِهِ تَحْيِيلاً وَهُوَ الغِطَاءُ، وَالكَشْفُ تَرْشِيحُ .
الأنبابي
قوله : (بِشَيْءٍ مُغَطَّى) كالعروس.
His statement: (and from subtle understanding... etc.) The waw enters upon his statement: 'unveils', and the idhafa in his statement: 'subtle understanding' is from the idhafa of the adjective to the described, and 'understanding' (al-fahm) means 'the understood thing' (al-mafhum). The estimation then is: 'and he unveils the cover from the subtle understood thing.' And in his speech there is an isti'ara bi-al-kinaya and takhyil, because he likened subtle understanding to a covered thing, a simile implicit in the mind. He omitted the name of the likened-to thing and affirmed something of its concomitants as an imaginative detail, which is the cover, and the 'unveiling' is tarshih (reinforcement).
Al-Anbabiy: His statement: (to a covered thing) like a bride.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage explains the second hemistich of the matn line. It clarifies the grammar: 'wa' enters on 'yakshifu', and the idhafa in 'daqiq al-fahm' is an adjective-noun phrase, with 'fahm' meaning 'mafhum' (the thing understood). So the meaning is 'unveils the cover from the subtle understood thing.' Then the commentator identifies a rhetorical figure: isti'ara bi-al-kinaya (metaphor by implication). The subtle understanding is implicitly compared to a covered object; the cover (al-ghita') is a necessary concomitant of that covered object, mentioned as takhyil (imaginative detail), and the act of unveiling (kashf) is tarshih (reinforcement of the metaphor). Al-Anbabiy adds an example: like a bride (who is covered). Thus the verse is not just literal; it uses a poetic metaphor to express that logic reveals deep intellectual meanings.

Key Terms
دقيق الفهم
استعارة بالكناية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri's commentary, what does the word 'ghita' (cover) represent in the metaphor?
A) The actual cover of a book
B) A concomitant of the implicit likened-to thing (a covered object)
C) The subject of logic
D) A rhetorical term for 'truth'

Key Takeaway
In logic's definition, the verse uses an implicit metaphor: subtle understanding is like a covered thing; logic unveils it, which is reinforced by the cover (takhyil) and the act of unveiling (tarshih).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify an isti'ara bi-al-kinaya in another definition from logic or usul al-fiqh (e.g., 'al-qiyas huwa al-mustanbitu' fi al-ahkam' might involve a metaphor). Write down the implicit simile and the concomitant mentioned.
?
Explain how al-Bajuri's use of takhyil and tarshih in this verse reinforces the idea that logic is an active tool for uncovering hidden knowledge.

Understanding Rhetorical Resumption and Pronoun Reference
Bajuri explains the rhetorical resumption and pronoun reference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the isti'naf bayani and determine the correct referent of pronouns in a logical commentary passage.

Core Idea
Commentary builds a dialogue: the isti'naf bayani answers an implied question.

In this passage, Bajuri explains why the matn calls the book a ladder. He uses a rhetorical device called isti'naf bayani, which resumes the explanation as if answering an unspoken question. Understanding this tool and tracking pronoun references is essential for following the commentator's logical flow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical question
Find the implied question that the phrase 'yurqa bihi' answers. Bajuri writes 'as if a questioner asked: What is the reason for naming it al-Sullam?'
This is the isti'naf bayani: the commentator resumes the explanation to clarify the reason for the name.
2
Trace the pronoun references
Identify the antecedents of the pronouns in 'yurqa bihi', 'sammaytuhu', and 'an yakuna khalisan'. Bajuri mentions two possibilities: the author or the book itself.
The pronoun 'bihi' can refer to the author (the one who named it) or to the book (the named thing).
3
Evaluate the two interpretations
Compare the two possible referents: (1) the author, as in al-Sharh al-Saghir, or (2) the book, as in al-Sharh al-Kabir. Bajuri prefers the first but acknowledges the second with a condition.
If referring to the book, it must be understood as the named thing, not the name, to avoid a conflict with the prior use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (يُرْقَى بِهِ ... إلخ) مُسْتَأنَفٌ اسْتِثْنَافاً بَيَانِيًّا، فَكَأَنَّ سَائِلاً قَالَ لَهُ: «مَا وَجْهُ تَسْمِيَتِهِ بِالسُّلَّم؟» فَقَالَ: «يُرْقَى بِهِ. إلخ . وَالصَّمِيرُ يَرْجِعُ لِلمُؤَلِّفِ الَّذِي رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ الضَّمِيرُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : سَمَّيْتُهُ ، وَكَذَلِكَ الضَّمَائِرُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : وَأَنْ يَكُونَ خَالِصاً ... إلخ»، كَمَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنَ الشَّرْحِ الصَّغِيرِ» لِلشَّيْخِ المَلْوِيِّ . وَيَصِحُ رُجُوعُ ذَلِكَ لِـ «السُّلَّمِ المُتَقَدِّمِ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ فِي الشَّرْحِ الكَبِيرِ) ، لَكِنْ يَتَعَيَّنُ أَنْ يُرَادَ بِهِ المُسَمَّى لَا الاِسْمُ ، كَمَا هُوَ المُرَادُ بِهِ فِيمَا سَبَقَ ، فَيَكُونُ فِيهِ اسْتِخْدَامُ، لَكِنَّ الأَوَّلَ أَوْلَى كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى . وَقَوْلُهُ : (سَمَاءُ عِلْمِ المَنْطِقِ) أَيْ : عِلْمِ المَنْطِقِ الشَّبِيهِ بِالسَّمَاءِ فِي العُلُوِّ ، فَإِضَافَةُ «سَمَاءِ» لِمَا بَعْدَهُ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المُشَبَّهِ بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّه . لا يُقَالُ : يَلْزَمُ عَلَى كَلَام المُصَنِّفِ تَوْصِيلُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ؛ لِأَنَّ هَذَا المُؤَلَّفَ بَعْضُ المَنْطِقِ، وَقَدْ جَعَلَهُ مُوصلاً لِعِلْمِ المَنْطِقِ، المُشْتَمِل عَلَى ذَلِكَ البَعْضِ . لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ : لَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ هَذَا المُؤَلَّفَ أَلْفَاظٌ لَا مَعَانٍ، فَلَا يَلْزَمُ مَا ذُكِرَ، وَعَلَى تَسْلِيم أَنَّهُ مَعَانٍ فَالمُرَادُ : أَنَّهُ يُرْقَى بِهِ لِمَا عَدَاهُ مِنْ عِلْمِ المَنْطِقِ، لَا لِجَمِيعِهِ الشَّامِلِ لَهُ.
His statement: (by which it is ascended ... etc.) is a resumed explanatory resumption, as if a questioner asked him: 'What is the reason for naming it al-Sullam?' So he said: 'By which it is ascended ... etc.' The pronoun refers to the author to whom the pronoun in his statement 'I named it' referred, and likewise the pronouns in his statement 'and that it be pure ... etc.', as taken from al-Sharh al-Saghir by al-Malwi. And it is valid for that to refer to the 'al-Sullam' mentioned earlier, as mentioned in al-Sharh al-Kabir, but it must be intended as the named thing, not the name, as was intended previously, thus there is a use [of the word for its meaning], but the first is better, as is not hidden. And his statement: (the sky of the science of logic) means the science of logic which resembles the sky in loftiness, so the addition of 'sky' to what follows is an addition of the analogized-to to the analogized. It cannot be said: There follows from the author's words that a thing leads to itself, because this authored work is a part of logic, and he made it a means of ascending to the science of logic which includes that part. For we say: It is not hidden that this authored work consists of words, not meanings, so what was mentioned does not follow. And on the assumption that it is meanings, the intended meaning is that it is ascended by it to the rest of the science of logic, not to its entirety that includes it.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's line 'yurqa bihi sama' 'ilm al-mantiq' meaning 'by which the sky of the science of logic is ascended.' The commentator first explains that the phrase is an isti'naf bayani, a clarification resumption answering a hypothetical question why the book is named 'ladder'. Then he discusses pronoun reference: the pronouns in the matn refer to the author (the matn writer) or to the book itself. He notes that it is possible to refer to the book as the named thing, not the name, but the first interpretation (referring to the author) is preferable. Then he explains the metaphor: 'sama' 'ilm al-mantiq' means logic is like the sky in loftiness; the construct is 'idafat al-mushabbah bihi ila al-mushabbah' (the analogized-to is added to the analogized). Then an objection is raised: If the book is a ladder to logic, but the book itself is part of logic, then it would be like leading the thing to itself. The answer is twofold: First, the book consists of words, not meanings, so it is not essentially identical to logic (which is a science of meanings). Second, even if it is considered meanings, the intended meaning is that it leads to the other parts of logic, not to the entire thing that includes it. This careful distinction preserves the metaphor without logical fallacy.

Key Terms
اسْتِثْنَاف بَيَانِيّ
إِضَافَة المُشَبَّه بِهِ لِلمُشَبَّه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the function of the phrase 'yurqa bihi' in the matn according to Bajuri?
A) It is a new independent statement.
B) It is an explanatory resumption answering an implied question.
C) It is a direct continuation of the previous sentence.
D) It is a correction of the previous statement.

Key Takeaway
Isti'naf bayani is a key tool in commentaries to answer unspoken questions, and tracking pronoun references is essential for correct interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find an example from a tafsir work (e.g., al-Tabari or Ibn Kathir) where a commentator uses a rhetorical question and answer to clarify an ayat. Identify the isti'naf bayani and explain what question it answers.
?
In Bajuri's passage, trace all pronouns and determine their antecedents. Write a brief analysis showing which interpretation is stronger and why.
